## Página 1
MANAGEMENT AND SUSTAINABILITY REPORT 2024
## Página 2
Banco de Occidente is a corporation with securities in 
the market through the trading system of the Colombian 
Stock Exchange for ordinary and subordinated bonds. As 
of December 31, 2024, $4.00T has been issued and $3.90T 
has been placed, of which $3.90T of series A Fixed Rate 
and B under IBR are still in force, with average opening 
and maturity terms being 2016 and 2028, respectively. 
At the end of 2024, the current issuance and placement 
program is $12.00T with an available limit of $6.00T to 
meet the needs of raising resources.
Likewise, Banco de Occidente’s shares are registered 
and traded on the Colombian Stock Exchange under the 
modality of ordinary shares.
City of principal domicile:  
Santiago de Cali, Valle del Cauca, Colombia 
Address of the main address:

Absenteeism: occurs when the worker does not 
attend or leaves his or her workplace, either with or 
without justification.

a flexible, dynamic and fast way to give productivity 
to teams.ADL Digital LAB: corresponds to a digital

Basel: are the international agreements or 
recommendations on banking supervision, issued 
by the Basel Committee on Banking Supervision 
Biodegradation: it is the ability of some materials 
to decompose naturally without human intervention.
Biodiversity: a term that includes the living species 
that provide the Earth’s life support system; a grouping 
of plants, animals, insects and fish make up the 
ecosystems that provide us with food, clean water, 
Bond: these are negotiable securities that represent 
a debt. Therefore, it can be said that when an investor 
acquires a bond, he is lending money to a company. 
The company that issues the bonds acquires the 
obligation to return to the holder of the bond (once 
the period established in it has elapsed) the amount 
of the investment plus a sum of money as interest 
(this is the investor’s return).
BPO: is the outsourcing of business process functions 
to service providers, either internal or external to the 
Braille: a reading and writing system made of raised 
dots used by visually impaired people to understand 
by touch with their fingers.
Carbon Footprint: indicator of impact on the 
environment due to the activities carried out by human 
beings with respect to the amount of resources used 
Carpooling: a term in the English language that 
means “sharing the vehicle” where several people 
travel on defined routes to the same destination and 
seeks to reduce the use of private vehicles with only 
one person on board.
Career Plan: it is the growth path defined so that 
employees can project their career at the Bank 
according to their competencies and expectations. 
It is articulated with our Corporate University and we 
are working on the construction of learning paths 
for each position.  Currently, the operational and 
commercial career plan is structured.  
CDC: in technology it corresponds to Change Data 
Capture, software that allows you to integrate, 
optimize and efficiently manage databases.
Coaching:  professional training of a person to 
achieve their goals through communication, self-
confidence, personal development and leadership.
Collective Investment Funds: mechanism or vehicle 
for savings or administration of sums of money or 
other assets, integrated with the contribution of a 
plural number of determinable persons once the 
fund comes into operation. These resources will be 
managed collectively to obtain collective economic 
Commercial Trust: legal transaction by virtue of 
which a person, called the settlor, transfers one or 
more specified assets to another, called the trustee, 
who undertakes to administer or dispose of them 
to fulfill a purpose determined by the constituent, 
for the benefit of the latter or a third party called 
beneficiary or trustee.
Collaborating Brand: talent recruitment, commitment 
and retention processes.
Contractor:  A person hired by the reporting 
organization to perform work that would otherwise be 
performed by a employees, at a workplace controlled 
by the organization.
Content Hub: web space where all the platform’s 
content converges, regardless of its format.
Credit Risk: possibility that one of the parties to a 
financial contract is unable to meet the financial 
obligations acquired; as a result, the other party 
Credit Scoring: is a credit evaluation methodology 
that consists of assigning a score to the potential 
debtor. In this way, the customer’s ability to pay is 
Critical Talent: positions of high impact and

Dale: is a digital wallet from Grupo Aval that allows 
users to send and receive money, make payments, 
make withdrawals at ATMs and refill balance easily 
and securely from their cell phone, without the need 
for a traditional bank account.  
Dashboard: tool or dashboard that reflects the 
management of performance indicators to monitor 
business objectives and processes.
Dematerialized Promissory Note:  security that 
supports credit operations that is not in physical 
form but by digital means.
Disability: disability is a concept that relates the 
sensory, physical, cognitive, intellectual, psychosocial 
and multiple differences that a person may have. 
This is articulated with the physical, attitudinal and 
communication barriers that limit their participation 
and access to different areas or work, social and 
economic contexts, among others.
Discrimination: are the actions or omissions that 
exclude, violate or affect in any way (physical, 
psychological, structural, among other forms of 
violence) a person because of their sexua orientation, 
gender identity, ethnicity, age, disability, place of 
origin, class or other marker of difference. 
Digital Ratio: in marketing, it corresponds to the 
percentage of interested parties who visit a website 
and stay doing the process that is being promoted.
Discharges: final disposal of liquids in bodies of 
water, soil or drains.
Diversity: refers to the multiple ways of being that 
characterize the groups and societies that make up 
humanity, it is manifested in the plurality of identity, 
social, cultural, ethnic and religious particularities, 
among others, that define each person and give 
added value to society.
Donation: a purely voluntary act by which a natural 
or legal person gives resources in money or in kind 
for the benefit of another, without obtaining anything 
Elderly: adulthood that begins from the age of 60; 
also classified as a senior citizen.
Electronic streamers: a physical self-service 
channel that makes it easier for the user to carry 
out transactions such as payments, inquiries and 
withdrawals, among others, with the use of the debit 
or credit card of Banco de Occidente or Grupo Aval 
Emotional Benefit: it is the one that the employees 
receives, in addition to their economic remuneration, 
related to their sensations and feelings with which 
they create a bond with the company or the brand.
Electronic Channels: mechanisms or options offered 
by our Bank to carry out transactions virtually. 
Electric Vehicle: car or land transportation that 
uses electricity for mobility, must be connected to 
Employees: a person who has a direct employment 
relationship with our Bank through a permanent 
or indefinite employment contract, and who fulfills 
obligations in exchange for remuneration that 
includes legal and extralegal benefits.
Employees Journey: measurement that allows 
us to know the traceability and performance of 
a employees in the company from their entry to 
Energy Efficiency: the ability to obtain the same 
or better results using the least amount of energy 
Finance for Biodiversity: a global initiative that 
seeks to mobilize the financial sector to support the 
conservation and restoration of biodiversity through 
responsible investments and sustainable strategies.  
FINDEV: is Canada’s development finance institution 
(DFI), which supports the private sector in developing 
markets to promote sustainable development.
Financed Emissions: are the greenhouse gas (GHG) 
emissions resulting from loans.
Fiscal Policy: policy established by the Bank 
regarding transparency and responsibility in tax 
Franchise: commercial contract by means of which a 
license is granted for the exploitation of a trademark 
Fusiondata: management system for government 
entities and whatever deemed necessary.  
Global Compact: UN initiative that encourages 
companies to adopt principles in human rights, labor 
standards, the environment and anti-corruption to 
promote sustainability and corporate responsibility. 
GPTW Certification: recognition granted by the 
Great Place To Work Institute and Icontec that 
certifies entities with high quality standards in the 
work environment and highlights the best places to 
work nationally and internationally.
Hybrid: A way of working that offers the possibility 
of working some days of the week from home and 
others in the offices. 
Hybrid Vehicle: Car or land transport that combines 
gasoline or diesel combustion with an electric motor 
IDB (Inter-American Development Bank): Multilateral 
organization whose objective is to offer financial 
solutions for the economic and social development 
Liquidity Risk: probability of incurring losses due to 
not having sufficient resources to meet the obligations 
Licenses: the right to use software or any other 
creation associated with a tracing language. 
Liquidity: A person or company’s ability to convert 
its assets into cash to cover its financial obligations.

Market Risk: Potential loss of the value of financial 
assets caused by adverse changes in the factors 
that determine their price.
Material Efficiency: corresponds to the metric of 
comparison between measures of cost, efficiency 
and flow of raw materials in their consumption, 
transformation and disposal to optimize processes.
Market Share:  in marketing, it corresponds to 
the indicator of market share or fraction that the 
organization has in a specific segment.
Materiality: in sustainability management, it 
corresponds to the environmental, social and 
governance aspects that the organization prioritizes 
based on the positive or negative impact on its 
MSCI Colcap: An index jointly created by MSCI and 
the Colombian Stock Exchange (BVC), it is designed 
to represent the performance of the Colombian 
stock market and aims to include a minimum of 25 
securities and 20 issuers based on free-float adjusted 
market capitalization, liquidity and international 
investment criteria.
Net Stable Funding Ratio (CFEN): corresponds to 
the ratio between the Stable Available Funding (FED) 
and the Required Stable Funding (FER), according 
to the definitions established by the Finance 
Superintendence of Colombia.
NEXA BPO: trademark of the affiliate Ventas y 
Omnichannel: refers to all touchpoints in the 
customer lifecycle – such as websites, social media, 
real-time chats, emails, phone calls, among others 
– work together, guaranteeing the user that their 
requirements are met quickly and seamlessly.
Openbanking: is a model that facilitates the 
exchange of information between all types of financial 
institutions through application programming 
interfaces (APIs). In this model, users are the owners 
of their financial information, therefore, they decide 
to share their data or not, with the aim of offering 
new products and services according to the needs 
Other Copyright: any other right that recognizes 
ownership over an invention in accordance with 
current regulations. 
Occupational Disease: Work-related injury, ailment, 
or illness that results in any of the following: Death, 
days off work, work restrictions or transfer to other 
positions, fainting or medical treatment beyond 
first aid, or serious injury or illness diagnosed by a 
physician or other certified health care professional, 
even if it does not result in the foregoing.
Occupational Accident: any unforeseen event 
at work that causes the worker an organic or 
psychological injury, disability or death.
Operational Risk: is the possibility that the entity 
incurs losses due to deficiencies, failures or 
inadequate functioning of processes, technology, 
infrastructure or human resources, as well as the 
occurrence of external events associated with them. 
It includes legal risk.
Occupational Risks: source or situation that can 
cause injuries or deterioration of health.
Organic Guidelines: corresponds to advertising 
(advertisements, news) or content that is disseminated 
by digital means at no cost.
PSE Button: digital tool that allows our customers 
to make payments and collections virtually and 
Public Trust: trust business that is entered into with 
public entities in accordance with the regulations 
applicable to the resources subject to the contract.
Private Equity Funds: are closed-end collective 
investment funds that must allocate at least two-
thirds of the contributions of their investors to the 
acquisition of assets or rights of economic content 
other than securities registered in the National 
Registry of Securities and Issuers -RNVE.
Payment Gateway: is the service that allows 
merchants to carry out customer collection operations 
by exchanging data between the seller’s bank and 
the buyer’s bank electronically (online), which allows 
the use of various payment methods (e.g. PSE, 
credit card, debit card and cash, among others). 
In addition, it provides value-added services such 
as the construction of the merchant’s website, the 
integration of payment buttons through Web Service 
or Apis, and enriched and online information.
Patents: industrial property right that recognizes the 
invention of a product or process, with an inventive 
level and industrial application. 
Pensioner: a person who is a beneficiary of a pension 
mainly for retirement, widowhood, disability or 
Parental Leave: leave granted by the company to 
employees who become fathers or mothers. Our Bank 
grants additional days to those stipulated by law.
Pet Friendly: offices that allow the entry and stay 
of pets (mainly dogs and cats) in the company of 
their owner so that they can carry out the activities 
Pricing: “assigning price” in English, is the process 
of setting the prices of products and services.
Prospects: person or company that shows interest 
in what the Bank is offering and becomes a target 
audience for the company’s product or service

Shares: a negotiable instrument that represents 
a proportional part of a company’s equity. It is a 
participation security, that is, when an investor 
acquires the shares of a company, he becomes a 
partner of the company. These instruments grant 
their holders economic and political rights that can 
be exercised collectively and individually.

Sponsorship: financial support given to an entity

Supplier: natural or legal person who offers products

Supply Chain: set of activities that involves 
everything from the purchase and transformation 
of raw materials to the manufacture, distribution 
and delivery of the product to the final consumer.
Stakeholders:  people or groups of people who

SOFR: The SOFR rate has been published by the

Waste: Anything that a person eliminates, wishes

## Página 9
We are pleased to present Banco de Occidente’s Management and Sustainability Report, reflecting 
our commitment to transparency, accountability and responsible management in the environmental, 
social and governance fields. This report summarizes the actions carried out by our bank in the 
period between January 1 and December 31, 2024 and has been prepared in reference to the 
Essential option of the GRI (Global Reporting Initiative) Standards and in compliance with Circular 
031 of 2021 of the Finance Superintendence of Colombia.
In its development, we identify the most relevant aspects of our sustainable management, highlighting 
the achievements reached and the goals that we continue to promote. As part of our commitment 
to transparency and continuous improvement, we have included the GRI Content Index, as well as 
the Sustainability Accounting Standards Board (SASB) sector indicators for the commercial banking 
industry. We also adopted the recommendations of the Task Force on Climate-related Financial 
Disclosures (TCFD), strengthening our climate disclosure strategy.
To guarantee the quality and reliability of the information presented, this report has been submitted 
to an Independent Limited Assurance process by the firm BDO Audit S.A.S. Regarding financial 
information, we have the tax audit of KPMG S.A.S. This external verification reaffirms our commitment 
to integrity, alignment with regulatory frameworks, and the adoption of international best practices.
The report also accounts for our contribution to sustainability at a global level, evidencing our 
voluntary management around the ten principles of the Global Compact and our participation in key 
initiatives such as the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs), the Dow Jones Sustainability Index 
(DJSI), the United Nations Environment Programme – Finance Initiative (UNEPFI), among others.
To facilitate the understanding of our contribution and compliance with these standards, we 
have included graphic references throughout the report, such as [GRI 2-25], [SASB FN-CB- 
410a.2] and the iconography of the SDGs, which allow us to clearly identify our commitment.

## Página 13
At Banco de Occidente, we have built a history of trust 
and soundness that has allowed us to accompany 
our customers, shareholders, employees and other 
stakeholders in their growth and evolution. Since 
our foundation in 1965 in Cali, we have developed 
innovative and sustainable financial solutions, 
adapting to the needs of the market and contributing 
to the progress of the country.
Today we have more than 175 branches, 18 Credit 
Centers and 3,093 ATMs in Colombia, in addition to 
our subsidiaries in Panama and Barbados. Over the 
years, we have evolved to offer innovative, sustainable 
financial solutions aligned with market needs. 
Our purpose is clear:  to make the development 
of people, the growth of businesses and the 
transformation of the country a reality. To achieve 
this, we are guided by four strategic pillars:

provides contact center and BPO services nationwide 
to entities from various economic sectors. Its strategic 
plan focuses on four fronts with nine objectives, aimed 
at maturing its service offering and diversifying its 
customer portfolio beyond its natural market, with a 
focus for 2025 on the growth of turnover in new and 
current customers, prioritizing competitive margins.

sustainability strategy, the diagnosis and benchmarking 
in sustainability, the fulfilment of strategic objectives 
through key indicators, the consolidation of the annual 
work plan, the development and execution of activities 
with ESG impact, the identification of material risks 
and the creation of the Sustainability Committee. 
During that same year, NEXA BPO promoted 
projects such as the Sustainability Ideathon, 
Recycling, Sustainable Fashion and carbon footprint 
measurement, while its main challenges included 
planning activities with greater impact, budget 
management and the review of the exclusive team 
for sustainability. Looking ahead to 2025, its strategic 
goals are to turn NEXA BPO into a BIC company, 
reduce its carbon footprint, update its sustainability 
purpose and strengthen its materiality strategy.
Its strategic plan focuses on four fronts with nine objectives, aimed 
at maturing its service offering and diversifying its customer 
portfolio beyond its natural market, with a focus for 2025 on 
the growth of turnover in new and current customers, prioritizing 
competitive margins. 
## Página 18
Fiduciaria de Occidente is a company dedicated to 
the execution of commercial trust agreements and 
non-transferable fiduciary mandates of ownership, 
whose fundamental purpose is to execute all kinds 
of commercial trust or trust contracts; receiving 
trust accounts; managing and investing their wealth 
to generate the best possible return; acting as a 
representative or agent of interests of third parties 
for any purpose; managing assets and investments, 
representing holders of bonds or any other securities 
issued in series; managing guarantees constituted 
by third parties; and managing authorized collective 
investment funds, including private equity funds, entering 
into all other transactions permitted to trust companies. 
Its strategic plan, designed to consolidate leadership in 
the fiduciary sector through innovative and sustainable 
strategies, is aimed at improving the customer experience, 
optimizing processes and expanding its portfolio of 
services, based on strategic objectives that include 
sustainable growth, customer satisfaction, reliability and 
the well-being of its people. The corporate strategy is 
based on three pillars: innovation and transformation, 
alignment with Banco de Occidente and vocation for 
With a direct presence in six regional offices nationwide 
(Barranquilla, Santa Marta, Montería, Medellín,

liabilities of $38,812,040,800.08, operating

2024 was characterized by being a year with a slow 
moderation of inflation, without a significant economic 
slowdown. In developed economies, the slowdown in 
inflation allowed central banks to begin normalizing 
their monetary policy, although inflation remains at 
above-target levels.  
Regarding the behavior of the markets, during the first 
half of 2024 the volatility was mainly explained by the 
dynamics of the labor market in the United States, as 
concerns arose of an economic slowdown in the country 
as a result of the increase in unemployment, however, 
these concerns faded as the American economy 
continued to grow at a solid pace and the labor market 
remained stable, which allowed volatility to moderate. 
In addition to this, another event that generated stress 
in the markets and significant movements was what 
occurred on August 5 on account of the Bank of Japan’s 
(BoJ) decision to surprisingly increase its interest rate by 
115 bps to 0.25% at the July 31 meeting, which resulted in 
a strengthening of the Yen against the dollar, which had 
reached lows not seen 38 years ago and caused many 
investors to leverage in Japan and the Yen to finance 
investments at low interest rates. However, when the 
BoJ surprisingly raised its interest rate, it deteriorated

## Página 27
The victory of the Republican Party was also in Congress; in the Senate they have 
a majority as they have 53 of the 100 seats. While in the House of Representatives, 
Republicans have 220 seats and Democrats have 215, more than 218 representatives 
are required in the House to have a majority. 
In this context, global equities end 2024 with strong valuations, mainly explained by 
the strength of the technology sector, in particular by companies related to Artificial 
Intelligence, microchips and semiconductors, where Nvidia was the company that stood 
out the most in the year and accumulated a valuation of 171%. With this, the Nasdaq 
index appreciated in 2024 by 25%, followed by the S&P500 (+24%). 
Investors were watching the labor market as the Federal Reserve kept interest rates 
high to tame inflation. Employment showed a slight deterioration with an unemployment 
rate that went from 3.7% at the end of 2023 to 4.1% as of December 2024. The Federal 
Reserve, based on contractionary monetary policy and high interest rates, sought to 
reduce inflation, however, it ran the risk of generating a significant deterioration of the 
economy and thus affecting employment, which is why, during the year, the employment 
results that end the year with a scenario of relative tranquility for Fed members and 
investors were of vital relevance.

On the other hand, inflation in the United States ended 2023 at 3.4% and did not decreased 
below 3.0% until July. In November, inflation was 2.7% and is expected to close the year at 
2.9%, showing that it is still persistent. With this, the Fed maintained a cautious stance for 
much of the year, keeping its interest rate stable in the range between 5.25% and 5.50% 
until the September meeting, in which it began its monetary policy normalization cycle, 
being the first cut in the interest rate in four years (they cut 50 bps). In addition, they made 
two cuts of 25 bps in the November and December meetings, with which the interest rate 
ended the year in the range between 4.25% and 4.50%.  
In Europe, the dynamics were marked by political uncertainty and limited economic growth, 
registering little significant variations compared to what was observed quarterly in 2023 and 
remained below 1% throughout the year, which still reflects a complex outlook. In Germany, 
the breakup of the governing coalition led to an early call for general elections to be held 
in February 2025. Meanwhile, in France, the parliament’s no-confidence motion against the 
prime minister, in a challenging political and fiscal scenario, further increased uncertainty.

## Página 28
As for Eurozone inflation, it moderated by 70 bps 
from 2.90% YoY observed in December 2023 to 2.20% 
YoY in November, continuing its path of corrections. 
Given the behavior of inflation, the ECB began its 
monetary policy normalization cycle at the June 
meeting and made 4 cuts throughout the year, with 
a decrease of 100 bps.  
Regarding China, the economy has failed to reach 
its 50% growth target, prompting the government to 
implement a series of fiscal and monetary stimulus 
packages to revive economic activity. This poor 
performance was especially affected by the crisis 
in the real estate sector, which continues to show 
no signs of recovery. 
On the monetary policy front, the People’s Bank 
of China (PBOC) kept its benchmark rates stable 
during the first half of the year until it decided to 
cut them by 10 bps in July, and in October it cut 
them by 25 bps, so that the prime rate on 1-year 
loans (LPRs) was reduced to 3.10% and the 5-year 
LPR was reduced to 3.60%. These movements are 
in line with the series of announcements made by 
the government of stimuli to boost the economy. 
Looking ahead to the coming months, there could 
be further cuts to boost economic activity. 
As for commodities, they showed a mixed behavior 
during 2024. The valuations are led by coffee (69.8%), 
gas (44.5%), gold (27.2%) and silver (21.5%), while the 
devaluations were led by soybeans (-22.1%), iron 
(-20.2%), cotton (-15.6%) and wheat (-12.2%).   
With coffee and other agricultural 
products such as cacao, these 
presented a good dynamic and 
traded at or near historical highs,  
this favored in particular the exporting 
countries of these products, such as 
Colombia, which contributed to a 
good dynamic of the primary sector.  
On the other hand, benchmark oil F Brent and WTI 
showed little variation. This was the result of a de-
escalation of tensions in the conflict in the Middle 
East, which resulted in crude oil supply remaining 
stable, in addition to concerns of weaker global 
demand due to economic dynamics in China and 
the gradual lifting of production cuts by OPEC+

Annual inflation peaked at 13.3% in March 2023, as 
of that date, inflation in annual terms has moderated, 
closing 2023 at 9.3%. During 2024, prices continued to 
grow at a lower rate, closing the year with a variation 
of 5.2%, with a drop of 407 bps compared to the 
The moderation in inflation is explained by a lower 
increase in prices in all divisions, particularly, the 
lines of goSDG and services that most influenced 
this dynamic were: i) Transportation: During 2023, 
a progressive series of increases in gasoline prices were made, which implied that the transportation item 
closed that year at 15.4%. In 2024 the increases in ACPM were moderate and their impact has not been 
significant, closing the year with a variation of 5.2%. ii) Food: The agricultural sector has been favored by 
moderate climatic phenomena, which has favored the production, distribution and marketing of food, with 
this, food inflation at the end of the year was 3.3%. iii) Rents and utilities: Rental prices have moderated, but 
gradually, limiting the accelerated correction of inflation, however, during the last few months, the special 
revision of utility rates in the Caribbean has supported the moderation of inflation. 
In line with the moderation in inflation, the Central Bank cut interest rates during 2024 and accumulated an 
adjustment of 350 bps in the year, going from 13.00% at the end of 2023 to 9.50% by the end of 2024 and, in 
December, surprised the market by moderating the speed of adjustment closing the year with a decrease of 
25 bps. Although inflation surprised to the downside during the second half of the year, Central Bank members 
opted for caution especially due to: i) inflationary risks derived from the depreciation of the exchange rate, ii) 
the persistence of fiscal uncertainty, and iii) the challenging international environment marked by the increase 
in risk premiums and expectations of restrictive financial conditions for longer time.      Local Context 
lThe balance for the country in 2024 was bittersweet. 
On the one hand, inflation continued its path of 
corrections, which allowed the Central Bank to move 
forward with the normalization of monetary policy.
This scenario favored the recovery of some sectors 
and contributed to the economy growing at a higher 
rate than in 2023. However, political and economic 
uncertainty was constant, compounded by concerns 
related to the country’s fiscal outlook.  
The economy grew 0.6% in 2023, showing a slowdown 
with greater effects on the construction sector 
(-4.1%) and industry (-3.6%) due to the moderation 
of dynamics due to the increase in interest rates, 
which limited household spending and reduced 
business investment. During 2024, economic activity 
has continued to grow, but at a moderate pace, 
from Occieconómicas we estimated that growth 
in 2024 would be between 1.6% and 1.8%, mainly

## Página 30
Regarding the exchange rate, the dollar in Colombia maintained a lateral movement 
with an average closing of $3,900 during the first 5 months of 2024, which was mainly 
explained by: i) the flow of dollars from large taxpayers for the payment of taxes, 
ii) Nutresa’s takeover bid and iii) the increase in oil prices. Then, the pair broke the 
psychological level of $4,000 to the upside in the middle of the year, mainly driven by 
the strengthening of the dollar worldwide as a result of the increase in geopolitical 
tensions in the Middle East, concerns of a possible economic slowdown in the United 
States and regional political uncertainty on account of the presidential elections 
in Mexico. Subsequently, in the second half of the year, the pair’s movement was 
influenced by: i) political and fiscal uncertainty at the regional level, ii) expectations 
of contractionary international financial conditions for longer, iii) the elections in the 
United States and the implications of Trump’s protectionist proposals, which reached 
a high during the year of $4,547 in November and closed the year at $4,405 with a 
year-average of $4,075.  
During 2024, the TES TF curve presented a steep movement with valuations of the 
TES 2025 of 57 bps and the TES 2026 of 8 bps, due to the decrease in interest rates 
of the Bank of the Republic and the government debt swaps. The rest of the curve 
was devalued by an average of 168 bps, a movement driven by the TES 2050 that 
rose in rate by 241 bps. In turn, the Ministry of Finance placed 1.05 T in TES 2046, the 
new reference started in the market at a rate of 11.50% and closed the year trading at 
12.78%. In this context, the difference between the TES 2025 and 2050 increased from 
96 bps at the end of 2023 to 395 bps at the end of 2024. For their part, the UVR TES 
end the year with an average devaluation of 125 bps, except for the UVR 2025 TES 
that are trading at 1.6% with a valuation of 170 bps.

Bank Changes and Results
We closed 2024 with an annual growth of 13.75% in 
total Assets, which grew by $8.73 trillion compared 
to December 2023, and reached a total balance 
of $72.65 trillion. The increase was mainly based 
on the growth of total Investment Financial Assets 
and Trading Derivatives, which reached the sum 
of $16.11 trillion, with a growth of 49.2% compared 
to the previous year, as a result of the execution 
carried out in Investments in debt securities where 
a year-year growth of 142.8% was evidenced with 
a positive variation of $4.87 trillion. 
This was followed by the growth of the Legal and 
Foreign Currency Gross Credit Portfolio (excluding 
Repos and Interbanks), which increased by $3.76 
trillion compared to the balance recorded in 
December 2023, equivalent to an annual increase 
of 8.6% and which contributed 43.1% of the growth 
According to the latest information available 
from the Finance Superintendence of Colombia, 
as of December 2024, Banco de Occidente has a 
market share of 7.23% in the total portfolio, (higher 
by 30bps from Dec-23). By type of portfolio, the 
Bank’s commercial portfolio closed at $33.6T, which 
represented an annual variation of 7.5% or $2.34 
trillion, and with a market share of 9.26% (higher by 
17bps from Dec-23). 
The consumer portfolio records an annual variation 
of $711.915 B, equivalent to an annual increase of 
5.8%, and a market share of 6.78% as of December 
2024, 60bps higher than Dec-23. Finally, the housing 
portfolio (Mortgage and Leasing) registered a year-
on-year growth of 18.5% and an annual variation 
of $479.271 B, the results are attributed to the good 
performance of the commercial force to promote 
the placement of credit products in the market.
The Credit Portfolio rated at C, D and E, registered a 
total balance of $3.17T, which represents 6.48% of the 
total gross legal and foreign currency credit portfolio 
and an annual variation of 10.01%. This behavior is 
mainly explained by the cyclical effects on the bank’s 
customers associated with the country’s economic 
behavior in which there has been an economic 
slowdown, inflation levels above the target range 
of the Bank of the Republic and the levels of interest 
rates in the Colombian market. The impact has been 
mainly concentrated in the consumer portfolio.  
On the side of total liabilities, our Bank closed 2024 
with a balance of $67.17T, registering a variation 
of $8.42T more than the balance at the end of the 
immediately previous year, which is equivalent to an 
annual percentage increase of 14.3%. 
Within the behavior of Total Liabilities, the performance 
presented in total deposits at the end of December 31, 
2024 stands out, which reached the sum of $48.18T, 
increasing by $3.20T compared to December 2023; 
which represents an annual percentage growth 
of 7.1%. This behavior is mainly explained by the 
evolution of savings accounts, which registered the 
sum of $23.69T with a growth of $4.16T compared 
to the same period of the previous year, equivalent 
to an annual percentage growth of 17.6%. Savings, 
checking accounts and CDTs represent 57.8%, 14.0% 
and 28.1% of the Bank’s total deposits, respectively. 
This accelerated growth of savings products is mainly 
explained by the Bank’s growth funding strategy in 
compliance with the different liquidity indicators 
(in particular CFEN) and the search to optimize the

Regarding Total Liabilities, at the end of 2024 they stood at $72.41T, representing a growth 
of 15.10% compared to the end of 2023, in response to the funding needs of our commercial 
operations. Total consolidated equity at the end of 2024 was $5.98T, up by $297.707B

Consolidated net income was $481.048B with a growth of 0.31% compared to 2023. The 
increase was mainly based on the growth of Net Other Income, which reached the sum of 
$770.495 B, with a growth of 63.67% compared to the previous year, mainly as a result of 
the net gain by difference in exchange where a year-on-year growth of $213.794 B was 
evidenced. The foregoing, followed by the 4.06% year-on-year variation in Net Interest 
Income and Valuation, equivalent to $90.756B, broken down between Interest Received on 
Credit Portfolio and Leasing Operations and Interest Expense on Deposits.
There was a variation of -4.54% compared to 2023 of Interest and Similar Expenses, represented 
in $249.412B, mainly explained by the variation in the component of Interest Expense on 
Deposits, which registered a year-on-year variation of -7.36%, as a result of the decrease 
in the volume of fundraising and monetary pressures that do not favor savings,  the increase 
compared to the end of 2023 by 6.12% of Financial Obligations is also noteworthy, which 
is equivalent to a variation of $70.297B.
The Other Net Expenditure item registered an increase of $182.031 B compared to 2023, 
which translates into a variation of 8.91%, in the breakdown of the variation, the increases 
in Personnel Expenditure of 9.42%, Depreciation and Amortization Expense (12.37%) and the 
increase in General Administration Expenses (9.79%) stand out.
## Página 35
Liquidity and Solvency 
In terms of the solvency indicator, during 2024 we continued with 
the analysis and development of different actions to strengthen 
the proactive management of its capital, managing to maintain 
an adequate level for compliance with regulatory indicators and 
internal risk appetite. The foregoing, within the framework of a 
higher level of capital required due to the increase of 38 basis 
points in the capital conservation buffer that all entities in the 
system must meet, and which in 2024 completed the transition 
period granted in accordance with the provisions of Article 13 
of Decree 1477 of August 2018.
Thus, at the end of 2024 we reached a total solvency indicator of 
12.70%, which meant an increase of 95 basis points compared to 
the end of 2023, as a result of (i) the strengthening of regulatory 
capital through the issuance of subordinated bonds abroad 
worth USD 175 million,  (ii) the internal generation of capital 
through profits, (iii) the permanent monitoring of assets 
weighted by credit risk level, and (iv) management of 
market and operational risk.
As relevant information, it is necessary to mention that we 
have been identified and declared a Systemically Important 
Entity – EIS for 2025, in accordance with resolution 2629 
of 2024 of the Finance Superintendence of Colombia – 
SFC. The status of an EIS requires the Bank to build an 
additional capital buffer equivalent to 1.0% of its assets 
weighted by credit, market and operational risk. To this 
end, the SFC granted a transition period to implement 
the new capital buffer in four stages as follows:

Free circulation of invoices 
In compliance with the provisions of Law 1231 of 2008 and 
added with Law 1676 of 2013, the Bank informs that it has 
no practices of withholding invoices from our suppliers, 
with the definition of internal policies to ensure the free 
circulation of invoices issued by vendors or suppliers.
Material transactions 
with related parties
To carry out transactions with related parties, we have procedures related to the 
MAN-COL-431 procedures manual, which establishes that operations carried out 
with customers classified as tied or related parties must have the approval of the 
Bank’s Board of Directors, for which there is a consultation list that allows the areas 
in charge to identify when a customer is part of this list. In addition, a monthly control 
is carried out on these operations to validate that the new active operations with 
tied and related parties have the due approval by the Board of Directors.
The details of these transactions are disclosed in note 28 of the separate FS and 
note 30 of the Consolidated FS.

## Página 46
With a clear commitment to boosting our country’s 
economy, we actively contribute to the development 
of society through timely tax contribution.  
This premise is evident in our Tax Policy [4], which 
reflects that our actions and the administration of 
tax matters are carried out with total transparency, 
clarity, order and coherence, always with a socially 
responsible vision of our stakeholders.
The Financial and Strategy Vice-Presidency is 
responsible for approving and modifying the 
organization’s fiscal strategy, but it is the duty of all 
our Bank employees and other interested parties to 
ensure compliance with the Fiscal Policy within the 
framework of its principles[5] of: Ethics, integrity and 
good practices, transparency, clarity,  coherence, 
prudence and legality.
At the Bank, all typical and atypical transactions or 
economic events are analyzed in a comprehensive 
manner, committed to complying with all current 
regulations, complementing them with the tax impact 
that they may represent, as part of our business 
strategy to prevent risks such as tax evasion.
On the other hand, we have controls such as 
compliance with the SOX Act[5] and the Operational 
Risk Management System Committee (SARO), 
which allow us to further shield our operations and 
contribute to our fiscal governance. We also carry 
out an annual audit that evaluates compliance in 
our management through an external tax auditor. 
The latter, in turn, is responsible for reviewing the 
declarations and submits an annual audit report. 
The tax audit helps us to identify possible errors 
and validate the correction of these to comply with 
legal requirements.
In terms of the annual income tax return, we have 
external tax advisors for the verification of the 
information presented, where the evidence of all 
the cases of the review such as audit reports and 
income reports, among others, remain.
In addition, we strengthen our processes for tax 
compliance through the training we carry out with 
recognized national associations and institutions 
such as Asobancaria, the National Association of 
Entrepreneurs of Colombia (ANDI), the Colombian 
Institute of Tax Law (ICDT), among others. With 
these activities we seek to update our entire team 
on the current regulations, laws, decrees, resolutions, 
jurisprudence and doctrines that apply to us. In this 
way, we strive for due compliance with regulations 
with the use of good practices and the analysis of 
strategies that support the execution of our work. 
This allows us to minimize some type of tax risk and 
guarantee the optimal tax burden.
We also participate in 
meetings with all our 
stakeholders, where 
opinions and concerns are 
raised in tax matters, as 
well as the action plans to be 
followed, which are recorded in 
minutes or informative emails. 
In addition, we participate 
in the Tax Committee of 
Asobancaria that meets 
ordinarily 12 times a year.

[5] For more information, see the Responsible Investment Practices topic of this Report.
[6] The Sarbanes Oxley Act (SOX) regulates the financial reporting and auditing of publicly traded companies.

## Página 49
As part of our comprehensive risk management,  we 
have designed a strategic structure that allows us 
to identify, assess and mitigate threats that could 
jeopardize our operational stability and financial 
sustainability. In this context, we also focus on 
preventing the materialization of negative impacts 
for our stakeholders.  
At the macroeconomic level, we are aware 
that instability in the banking sector can have 
broader consequences, such as the triggering 
of systemic economic crises that affect 
employment, investment and financial stability 
in the country, for this reason, comprehensive 
risk management becomes an essential pillar 
to safeguard the interests of our stakeholders 
and ensure the continuity of our operations.
In Colombia, the financial sector is subject 
to rigorous regulations, which means that 
the measures adopted to manage risks must 
be aligned with regulatory requirements and 
regulatory guidelines. In this sense, under 
the framework of the Comprehensive Risk 
Management System (SIAR) established by 
the Finance Superintendence of Colombia, 
we have defined the guidelines and actions 
necessary to manage the risks inherent to our 
operations. These risks include:
 B ank Book Interest Rate Risk
Our SIAR is made up of several fundamental 
stages to guarantee its effectiveness:
In this stage, the current and potential risks 
associated with the activities we carry out 
or that we plan to implement are identified.
We establish mechanisms to mitigate and 
reduce the likelihood of risks occurring, 
as well as to minimize their impact. 
In this phase, we evaluate and quantify 
the exposure to risks, as well as the impact 
they could have if they materialize, this 
measurement can be both qualitative and 
quantitative, depending on the type of risk.
We focus on the continuous monitoring 
of risk sources, the risk profile, deviations 
from established limits, and the effectiveness 
of the controls implemented.
## Página 50
As a complement to these actions and in line with our commitment to sustainable investments and with the full 
awareness that environmental and social risks can impact both our clients and society in general, since 2023 
we began the Environmental and Social Risk Management System (SARAS) which was fully implemented in 
July 2024. This system covers all segments and commercial management of Business Banking, and reinforces 
our ability to manage risks associated with environmental and social impacts, which could also affect our 
customers’ ability to pay.
Our comprehensive risk management is led by 
the Vice Presidency of Risk and Collection led by 
Fabian Mauricio Arias Jiménez and coordinates a 
specialized team composed of four managements 
and a directorate: Balance Sheet and Treasury 
Risk, Credit Risk, Operational Risk, Banking Security 
and the SOX Directorate, each unit is focused on 
a specific area of risk management, guaranteeing 
comprehensive and specialized coverage.
Responsibilities of the Vice Presidency of Risk and 
 In c oordination with the Holding Company 
Grupo Aval, it must define the risk indicators, 
limits and thresholds, in accordance with the 
organizational structure, business lines and 
guidelines established in our risk appetite 
statement, based on the methodologies and 
internal models defined.
 T he risk appetite, limits, thresholds and 
associated results are discussed and approved 
in several specialized committees, such as the 
Financial Risk Committee (Corporate Banking, 
Personal Banking), the Treasury Financial Risk 
Committee, the ALCO, the SARO Committee and 
the Risk Committee of Grupo Aval. These items 
are then submitted to the Board’s Comprehensive 
Risk Committee for consideration and approval.

## Página 51
Supervision falls on each of the Managers associated 
with the Vice Presidency of Risk and Collection, 
who present the results of their monitoring to the 
different risk committees. In addition, the Board’s 
Comprehensive Risk Committee (CIR), chaired by 
an independent Board member, meets quarterly to 
oversee risk management, monitor the risk profile, and 
ensure that policies and procedures are adequate.
Within its functions, the CIR advises the Board of 
Directors on operations, events or activities that 
may affect the exposure and risk profile, approves 
adjustments to the policies of the Comprehensive 
Risk Management System (SIAR), and continuously 
monitors the risk culture in the entity.
Comprehensive Risk 
Management Compliance
The Compliance Officer has the responsibility of 
overseeing the risk of money laundering, reporting 
directly to the Presidency and submitting detailed 
reports to the Board of Directors each quarter.  
Risk Management and 
Assessment Process
Our Manual: Comprehensive Risk Management 
System (SIAR) establishes the guidelines, parameters 
and internal procedures to guarantee adequate and 
comprehensive risk management in accordance 
with current regulations. Key elements of this system 
 Di sclosure of the SIAR and the Risk Appetite 
Framework (MAR) to the Board of Directors, 
senior management and business units.
 P eriodic review of the operation of the SIAR, 
with the updating of policies and procedures 
 T he definition and monitoring of thresholds and 
limits of the MAR, as well as the management 
of risks inherent to new markets and activities.
 T he implementation of corrective measures in 
the event of deviations and the evaluation of 
their effectiveness.
 Oper ational risk management and the 
contracting of insurance and third parties for the 
development of processes, without delegating 
the professionalism of risk management.

their respective controls, among them we highlight:  
Information Security and Computer Security

accounts, and cybersecurity.

KPMG annually carries out an internal 
audit where it reviews the management of 
the different types of risks, in these audits 
we have obtained generally satisfactory 
results on all fronts, when opportunities for 
improvement are identified, each risk specialty 
develops action plans to close the gaps 
detected. These plans are monitored by the 
aforementioned external auditor and reported 
both to the risk committee of each specialty 
and to the comprehensive risk committee of 
the board of directors. Similarly, our holding 
company has a corporate comptroller that 
periodically evaluates the risk management 
of the different entities.

Incorporation of Risk 
Criteria in New Products
In accordance with the regulations of the Finance 
Superintendence of Colombia, the identification 
of risks is carried out prior to the launch of new 
products, services, or technologies, as well as 
the incursion into new markets. The risk of money 
laundering, terrorist financing and arms proliferation 
is integrated into all our new projects through risk 
analysis and the establishment of specific controls. 
The Balance Sheet and Treasury Risk Management 
actively participates in the development of new 
products, validating valuation methodologies and 
evaluating the impact on risk metrics.
This comprehensive approach allows risks to be 
managed effectively and ensures that each new 
project or product conforms to the principles of 
prudence, control and regulatory compliance.
## Página 53
At Banco de Occidente we analyze emerging 
risks through the PESTAL methodology which 
analyzes Political, Economic, Social, Technological, 
Environmental and Legal factors, through which 
we were able to identify how climate change and 
artificial intelligence and new technologies focused 
on criminal activities, both in Colombia and globally, 
can have a significant impact on the local economy 
and that of our clients in the next 3 to 5 years.
Emerging risk Category Potential impact Mitigation actions
TTaking into account that our bank customers belong to different 
sectors, in the event of an effect generated by this risk, we may be 
affected in the non-payment of obligations due to the damages 
suffered, deterioration and/or interruption of operations. 
Increased losses in portfolio exposed to sectors vulnerable to 
extreme weather events.
In addition, we may present an increase in market risk due to 
the Bank’s lack of alignment with the sustainable preferences 
Therefore, as an entity we seek to integrate climate risks with our 
bank’s risk management model, with early warnings and mitigation 
measures through which we can provide our customers with 
better support and the satisfaction of their needs by reducing 
environmental risks.
At the Bank, we have carried out a diagnosis of the impact of the 
risk and we have a preliminary action plan which is being carried 
out with the consulting firm Deloitte to update the diagnosis, 
define the governance structure and develop the action plan 
to mitigate the estimated potential impact.
During the last 30 years we have valued more than 3,400 
initiatives, encouraging the conservation and care of water, 
the principle of life. Likewise, we continue with the development 
of initiatives to mitigate and adapt to climate change.
Currently, due to the great scope that this risk has in our sector, 
we can be strongly impacted by the theft of information through 
applications, loss of money due to identity theft, theft of confidential 
information through emerging technologies installed in frequently 
used devices, kidnapping of information and extortion for its 
This risk is thus reflected in the materialization of fraud, the loss 
of customer information and confidential information of the 
bank, thus leading us to the materialization of reputational risk 
due to the impact on the service.
We are working on the implementation of communication 
strategies for customers and employees focused on preventive 
actions and confirmation of authenticity in the face of possible 
requirements through artificial intelligence, in addition we are 
strengthening the authentication schemes for customers and 
employees in channels and services provided by the Bank.
To mitigate everything related to the risk of new technologies 
focused on criminal activities, as a bank we are using technologies 
to protect against malware attacks on the devices of customers 
and employees, we are also raising awareness about the risks 
and threats to which customers and employees may be exposed 
in the event of bad practices in the use of technologies and 
implementation of cybersecurity tools that prevent attacks 
from accessing the Bank’s infrastructure in cases of deception

Our Credit Risk Management is carried out through 
the Credit Risk Management System (SARC), which in 
turn is part of the Comprehensive Risk Management 
System (SIAR), and includes the policies, procedures 
and methodologies established for the proper 
management of this risk in the bank’s portfolio.
By December 2024, the total Bank portfolio totals 
$48.99 trillion with an annual growth of 7.89% and 
is distributed 67.64% in the commercial portfolio, 
26.17% in the consumer portfolio and 6.19% in the 
housing portfolio. The portfolio growth by type of 
credit compared to December 2023 was: commercial 
7.81%, consumer 5.81% and housing 18.75%.
At the product level, the commercial portfolio is thus 
composed of 70.64% by ordinary portfolio, 18.16% 
by leasing, 8.43% by treasury, 1.73% by Unidirecto,

other hand, in the consumer portfolio, the product 
with the highest participation is payroll loans with 
43.20%, followed by personal loans with 28.28%,

revolving credit with 0.32%.

and air conditioning; water distribution; wastewater 
evacuation and treatment, waste management

($2,564,530 MM). The other 13 economic activities 
represent the remaining 45.18%.

## Página 55
Evaluation and Measurement  
In the granting of credit we have different models 
for risk assessment with internal scoring models for 
the evaluation of the consumer portfolio. In the initial 
evaluation of operations, models are applied that 
assign a score to the customer based on bureau 
variables, as well as behavioral variables with the 
sector that allow establishing whether the applicant 
is subject to credit in accordance with the Bank’s 
policies on the minimum score required. There are 
monitoring models that mainly use variables of 
customer payment behavior and use of products 
that allow customers to be qualified and establish 
the probability of default occurring during the next 
For the commercial portfolio we have rating models, 
whose variables are primarily financial indicators 
that are obtained from the financial statements 
delivered by customers, with these variables the 
input models are obtained and for the monitoring 
models, they are considered variables of payment 
behavior. As described above, there are entry and 
monitoring models for the segments of Industry, 
Commerce, Services, Construction Companies, 
Territorial Entities and Financial Entities. Among other 
uses, these models are used in the credit granting 
process for the classification of customers, in the 
determination of the amount to be loaned, in the 
structuring of commercial placement programs, and 
in monitoring, for the qualification of the portfolio 
and the estimation of provisions, as well as in the 
monitoring of the composition of the portfolio by risk.
Exposure limits by economic sector in the commercial 
portfolio are monitored quarterly, where by December 
2024, 100% of the sectors are within the established 
appetite. In the consumer and housing portfolios, 
monthly monitoring is carried out such as the Through 
The Door - Policy Monitoring Score by product and 
the analysis of disbursements by variables, which 
reflect the evolution of the harvests, from which 
adjustments have been made in policies to improve 
the performance of the portfolio.
Management, Monitoring 
The credit risk models applied in the commercial 
and consumer portfolio are monitored biannually 
(June and December) in terms of the ability to 
discriminate customers with good behavior and 
bad payment behavior through Backtesting. The 
Accuracy-Ratio (AR) indicator is considered as a 
measure of goodness of fit. In case the AR is at least 
50%, the model remains in production, while if the 
AR is less than 50%, a new credit risk model must 
As part of the monitoring, in 2024 we carried out an 
analysis of the impact of exchange rate risk on our 
customers, showing that good behavior continues to 
be observed in customers with an import vocation, 
since capital presents a growing trend and despite 
the increase in the overdue, the ICV is at very low 
Our portfolio in foreign currency increases its balance 
a little and keeps the levels of non-performing loans 
and risk low, due to this during 2024 we monitored 
international behavior, with analysis of economic 
growth and inflation, to understand the possible 
effects and repercussions in the country. 
Similarly, we carried out national analyses, specifically 
in sectors affected by situations such as the La Niña 
phenomenon, government reforms, input prices, 
among others; identifying the exposure in these 
sectors, the number of customers and how the 
dynamics of the portfolio could be affected. The 
results of these analyses have led us to conclude 
that exposure to customers and sectors with possible 
impacts is low and controlled. 
Likewise, during the year we monitored the granting 
policies by score, profile and risk nodes for each of 
the products, where they have shown satisfactory 
results with respect to the 2023 harvests, presenting 
a decrease in overdue and non-performing loan 
We also made the cross-selling of credit cards and 
payroll loans more flexible, as well as credit cards 
and personal loans. Likewise, the youth credit card 
had an adjustment, in which a decrease was made in 
the cut-off points, among others. At the end of 2023, 
the implementation of all products in the decision 
engine was completed, with vehicles being the last to 
be incorporated. This has allowed for a more timely 
and efficient administration of granting policies, as 
well as the administration of placement campaigns 
and adequate monitoring of portfolio performance. In 
addition, the implementation of the Decision Engine 
leveraged a greater dynamic of Campaigns in the 
Personal Banking portfolio.
## Página 56
Country Risk Management
The country risk management system allows us to determine the need to have impairment provisions on 
capital investments abroad. The foregoing corresponds to Banco de Occidente’s investments in Banco de 
Occidente (Panama) S.A. and Occidental Bank Barbados Ltd.
In accordance with the provisions of the SIAR, in 2024 we carried out updates to the country risk assessment. 
This study assigns a rating to countries in which capital investments are made abroad, which is composed 
of a base analysis that includes financial, economic and market indicators, and a complementary analysis 
that focuses on political, institutional, social and projection aspects, complemented by the ratings of the 
risk rating agencies. 
Given that our investment in foreign subsidiaries is in Banco de Occidente Panama - BOP and Occidental Bank 
Barbados - OBB, entities through which we have portfolios and investments outside Panama and Barbados, 
the country risk classification (A, B, C, D, E) of these two jurisdictions, in accordance with our policy, can be 
improved by taking into account the weighted average of the ratings of the countries where the exposure 
is located. According to the results of the latest update, the countries where we currently have investments 
obtained the following rating: Panama and Barbados B.
Therefore, and following the policy established by the Bank, it is concluded that, according to the rating 
obtained in both countries, no provisions are required for impairment of these investments.

the Basic Accounting and Financial Circular in its part

risks through identification, measurement, control 
and monitoring. In this regard, we are constantly 
working on updating the risks and controls in the 
processes, monitoring the risk profile and following 
up on the record of operational risk events, which 
allows the implementation of corrective actions 
aimed at mitigating the materialization of events, 
reducing the levels of exposure to operational risks 
and the result of exposure to operational risk which 
is part of the solvency relationship.

In accordance with the External Guide for the 
Supervision of Conduct Risk, issued by the Finance 
Superintendence of Colombia on September 24, 
2024, our bank implemented the Conduct Risk 
Management System, recognizing the importance 
of properly managing these risks to protect the rights 
of financial consumers and maintain confidence in 
the financial system.
Conduct risk is defined as the possibility of affecting 
the rights of the financial consumer or the market, 
derived from a practice of a supervised entity. In 
this regard, our bank has implemented a conduct 
risk management system, which includes policies, 
procedures and methodologies designed to promote 
fair, transparent and ethical practices in all our 
operations, ensuring that our products and services 
are aligned with the needs and expectations of our 
Since 2024, we have carried out the process of 
implementing this system, continuously reporting to 
the Board of Directors on its progress and evolution. 
 To identify conduct risks, we carry out an analysis 
based on the operational risk matrix and identify the 
processes involved in the life cycle of our financial 
products and services. From this analysis, we have 
identified the conduct risks to which our financial 
consumers are exposed and their potential impact. 
To this end, we consider the pillars of the Consumer 
Service System (SAC) defined in Law 1328 of 2009, 
the database of complaints filed by consumers in 
the last year, and the classification of risk factors 
and their causes established in the External Guide 
for Supervision of Conduct Risk of the Finance 
As of December 2024, 139 risks and 526 controls were 
identified. However, during 2025, a purging process 
has been carried out to optimize the management 
of these risks, prioritizing those with the greatest 
impact on the customer.
Finally, our bank promotes a customer-centric 
organizational culture, supported by continuous 
training programs for our employees, with the aim 
of preventing possible effects and strengthening 
trust with our users. These actions are aligned with 
the commitment to mitigate the conduct risk.
Business Continuity Plan
During 2024, we continued with the work of 
permanently updating the Continuity model (updating 
strategies, process tests, business impact analysis 
(BIA), and call tree), as well as monitoring compliance 
with service level agreements for their respective 
Likewise, aiming to strengthening the business 
continuity management system, we began the first 
phase of implementation of the contingency scheme 
under the Full VPN mechanism, where the employees’ 
house functions as a contingency operation center 
for the Bank’s critical processes, this in order to have 
an additional alternative to our current scheme and 
thus have more tools in the face of crisis events that 
At the technological level, throughout 2024 we 
executed activities on the infrastructure that supports 
the Bank’s critical applications and we were able to 
operate some applications in the Alternate Computer 
Center, guaranteeing that, in the event of a service 
failure in the main computer center, the banking 
operation would be continued. 
Finally, and in order to comply with External Circular 
042 of 2012 of the Finance Superintendence, we 
monitored the continuity plans of third parties that 
provide us with critical services, a scheme that has 
been strengthened with the support of Asobancaria.
The Parent Company manages liquidity risk in 
accordance with the standard model established 
in Chapter XXXI (annexes 9 and 12) of the Basic 
Accounting and Financial Circular of the Finance 
Superintendence of Colombia and in accordance 
with the basic principles of the Comprehensive Risk 
Management System (SIAR), which establishes the 
## Página 59
minimum prudential parameters that entities must 
implement in their operation to efficiently manage 
the liquidity risk they are exposed to. 
To measure liquidity risk, the Parent Company 
calculates a Liquidity Risk Indicator (IRL) on a 
weekly basis for terms of 7, 15, 30 and 90 days, as 
established in the standard model of the Finance 
Superintendence of Colombia and on a quarterly 
basis for its subsidiaries to measure the liquidity risk 
of the conglomerate. 
In addition, the Parent Company measures monthly 
the stability of its funding in relation to the composition 
of its assets and positions outside the statement of 
financial position, over a one-year horizon through 
the net stable coefficient (CFEN), as established in 
the standard model of the Finance Superintendence 
On a daily basis, we monitor the availability of 
resources not only to meet reserve requirements, but 
also to foresee and/or anticipate possible changes 
in the Parent’s liquidity risk profile and to be able to 
make strategic decisions as appropriate. In this sense, 
the Parent has liquidity early warning indicators that 
allow establishing and determining the scenario 
in which it finds itself, as well as the strategies to 
be followed in each case. Such indicators include 
the level of high-quality liquid assets, the levels of 
concentration of deposits, the use of liquidity limits 
of the Bank of the Republic, among others.
Through the technical committees on assets and 
liabilities (Finance and ALCO Committee) and the 
Comprehensive Risk Committee of the Board of 
Directors, the Bank’s senior management is aware 
of the liquidity situation and makes the necessary 
decisions taking into account the high-quality 
liquid assets that must be held, the tolerance in 
the management of liquidity or minimum liquidity,  
strategies for granting loans and raising funds, 
policies on the placement of surplus liquidity, changes 
in the characteristics of existing products as well as 
new products, diversification of sources of funds 
to avoid the concentration of deposits in a few 
investors or savers, hedging strategies, the results 
of the Parent Company and changes in the balance 
In terms of Liquidity Risk management, during 2024, 
we had a sufficient level of liquid assets to meet 
short-term liquidity requirements. In accordance with 
the above, under SFC methodology, liquid assets and 
30-day liquidity requirements stood at an average 
of $8.6 trillion and $6.2 trillion respectively, yielding 
a ratio of 139.3% that is comfortable with respect 
to the appetite limit (minimum 120.0%) defined by 
the Bank and well above the legal limit (minimum 
100.0%). In ALM management, we highlight the 
permanent monitoring of early warning indicators, 
which generally had a stable behavior within the 
established appetite limits.

Qualitative Analysis  
We participated in the monetary, foreign exchange 
and capital markets in the search to satisfy its needs 
and those of its customers in accordance with the 
established policies and risk levels. In this regard, 
we manage different portfolios of financial assets 
within the permitted limits and risk levels.
Market risk arises from the entity’s open positions in 
investment portfolios in debt securities and derivative 
instruments, from adverse changes in risk factors 
such as interest rates, inflation, foreign currency 
exchange rates and their volatility, as well as in the 
liquidity of the markets in which it operates.
At Banco de Occidente we negotiate financial 
instruments with several objectives, among which 
the following stand out:
 O ffer products tailored to the needs of customers, 
which fulfill, among others, the function of 
covering their financial risks.
 S tructure portfolios to take advantage of 
arbitrages between different curves, assets 
and markets and obtain returns with adequate 
capital consumption.
 C arry out operations with derivatives, for 
intermediation purposes with clients or to 
capitalize on arbitrage opportunities, both 
exchange rate and interest rates in the local 
and foreign markets.
In carrying out these operations, we incur risks 
within defined limits or mitigate them with the use of 
operations of other derivative financial instruments.
## Página 63
The risks assumed in carrying out operations are 
reflected in a structure of limits for positions in 
different instruments according to their specific 
strategy, the depth of the markets in which they 
operate, their impact on the weight of assets by 
risk and level of solvency, as well as the balance 
These limits are permanently monitored and reported 
daily to senior management, biweekly to the Finance 
Committee, monthly to the Risk Committee and 
quarterly to the Board of Directors (Integral Risk 
Market risks are quantified through value-at-risk 
models (internal and standard). The Boards of 
Directors approve a structure of limits based on 
the value at risk associated with the annual profit 
budget and establish additional limits by type of risk.
We use the standard model for measuring, controlling 
and managing the market risk of interest rates and 
exchange rates in the treasury and bank books. 
These measurements are carried out on a daily basis 
in the case of the Parent Company and monthly for 
each of its subsidiaries to measure and monitor the 
conglomerate risk.
We currently map the active and passive positions of 
the treasury book, within zones and bands according 
to the duration of the portfolios, the investments in 
collective portfolios and the net position (assets 
minus liabilities) in foreign currency, both in the bank 
book and the treasury book, in line with the standard 
model recommended by the Basel Committee.
Likewise, the Parent Company has parametric internal 
management models based on the Value at Risk (VaR) 
methodology, which have allowed it to complement 
market risk management by identifying and analyzing 
variations in risk factors (interest rates, exchange 
rates and price indices) on the value of the different 
instruments that make up the portfolios. These models 
are JP Morgan’s Risk Metrics.
The methodologies used to measure VaR are 
periodically evaluated and subjected to performance 
tests to determine their effectiveness. In addition, at 
the Bank we have tools to carry out stress tests and/
or sensitization of portfolios under the simulation of 
extreme scenarios.
The entity’s senior management and Board of Directors 
actively participate in risk management and control 
through the analysis of an established reporting 
protocol and the conduct of various Committees, 
which comprehensively carry out monitoring, both 
technical and fundamental, of the different variables 
that influence the markets internally and externally  
to support strategic decisions.
Likewise, the analysis and monitoring of the different 
risks incurred by the entity in its operations is essential 
for decision-making and for the evaluation of 
results. On the other hand, a permanent analysis of 
macroeconomic conditions is essential in achieving 
an optimal combination of risk, profitability and 
## Página 64
The ∆MNI has a short-term approach, since it 
measures the impact of the shock scenario for the 
one-year horizon and under the assumption of 
constant balance sheet, i.e., that there is no growth 
or decrease in balance sheet positions. This metric 
reflects the impact on net interest income under 
a parallel shock of +/- 400 bps. In addition, the 
sensitivity for a parallel shock of +/- 100bps is 
The ∆VEP has a long-term approach and under the 
assumption of balance sheet in liquidation, that is, 
the total time horizon until the last maturity of the 
positions on the balance sheet is evaluated. This 
metric includes, under different scenarios, the change 
in the present value of interest-rate sensitive assets 
Bank Book Interest 
Bank book interest rate risk is defined as “present or 
prospective risk to the entity’s capital and earnings 
arising from adverse movements in interest rates 
and affecting bank book positions.” Likewise, Bank 
Book Credit Spread Risk (RSCLB) is defined as “any 
type of credit spread and liquidity spread risk that is 
not explained by the RTILB, nor by credit risk”. At the 
Bank, we have defined within our policies that this 
risk is only applicable to bank book positions that 
do not consume capital due to market risk, including 
transactions of assets, liabilities and off-balance 
sheet items that have this exposure.
In this sense, we have exposure to interest rate 
fluctuations that impact future cash flows. The risk 
may arise due to the mismatch in the repricing time 
between assets, liabilities and off-balance sheet 
positions, the use of different interest rates (IBR, 
DTF, SOFR, Fixed, etc.) and the options that may 
generate changes in the cash flows of both the active 
or passive positions made by the Bank (for example,  
prepayments). Interest margins can be increased 
or reduced as a result of changes in interest rates, 
bringing with them impacts on the institution’s results, 
however, at the Bank we have mechanisms such 
as hedging through derivative instruments to deal 
with the risks associated with the interest rate in the 
At the Bank, we manage the Bank Book Interest Rate 
Risk (RTILB) in accordance with the standard model 
established in Chapter XXXI (annex 15) of the Basic 
Superintendence of Colombia, which establishes the 
supervise in their operation to efficiently manage 
To measure the RTILB, we calculated two indicators, 
the ∆VEP (economic value of equity) under six shock 
scenarios (parallel up, parallel down, flattening, 
steepness, rise in the short, fall in the short) and the 
∆MNI (net interest margin), under two interest rate 
shock scenarios (parallel up and parallel down), as 
and liabilities and, therefore, their final impact on 
the economic value of equity.
According to the regulatory framework, the SFC 
requires that the maximum value of sensitivity to 
the VEP under the six interest rate shock scenarios 
be below 15% of the sum of the Ordinary Basic 
Equity (PBO) and the Additional Basic Equity (PBA). 
Therefore, the Bank monitors compliance with this 
indicator, and has a risk appetite statement, which 
is monitored on a monthly basis.  
The results obtained in the measurement of sensitivity 
to the VEP and the MNI for the cut-off December 31, 
2024 are presented below, where it is evident that 
the Bank is within the defined appetite (maximum 
9.00% according to internal thresholds) and has 
slack with respect to the regulatory limit (15.00%).
## Página 65
In addition, the results obtained around the RSCLB for 
the same evaluation period are recorded. Based on 
historical information and for a scenario of interest 
rate hikes, the Bank (for a three-month period) has 
a probability of loss of $98.247B for investments 
classified as available-for-sale that are not delivered 
as collateral in central counterparty risk or in the 
development of money market operations (repos, 
buyback/sellback or temporary transfer of securities).
The management of the RTILB, which 
incorporates credit differential risk 
and RSCLB liquidity spread, is the 
responsibility of the ALM Management 
and the Balance Sheet and Treasury 
Risk Management; however, through 
the ALCO committee, strategies are 
defined that involve the Financial 
Planning area and the commercial 
areas, allowing the objectives 
proposed by the Bank to be met and 
keeping the RTILB within the defined 
These results are based on the fact that the Bank’s cumulative reprice gap does not present a significant 
mismatch and therefore the exposure to bank book interest rate risk (RTILB) is not significant when evaluated 
from the sensitivity to the economic value of equity (VEP). When the duration of the asset and liability are 
close, a change in interest rates affects both balance sheet items in similar proportions. This allows us to 
conclude that maintaining a repricing structure with a not so wide mismatch is a way of protecting the value 
of the entity’s equity.
