## Página 66
In the case of the 2024 Stress Tests as regulated in Circular Letter 028 of 2024, four 
scenarios were defined: the Base scenario, which corresponds to a context in which 
the economy and the financial system do not suffer unexpected shocks; an adverse 
scenario, which constitutes a hypothetical context in which the economy and the 
financial system are affected by unexpected shocks which are severe enough to 
produce breaches in the minimum regulatory requirements of solvency and liquidity; 
an adverse scenario with climate risk (rainfall), which adds to the events of the adverse 
scenario, the materialization of acute physical risks derived from climate change; and 
an adverse scenario with mitigating factors, which preserves the macroeconomic 
assumptions of the adverse scenario, but including the mitigating actions carried 
out by the Bank to increase its solvency and liquidity levels above regulatory limits. It 
should be noted that the adverse scenario is totally hypothetical in its construction to 
model non-compliance with the regulatory solvency and CFEN (Net Stable Funding 
Ratio) and is not foreseeable to occur in the medium and long term.
For this EPR (Stress Test Scheme) exercise that we carried out and in accordance 
with what was defined by SFC (Finance Superintendence of Colombia), it is based 
on information from balance sheet figures at end of December 2023 and is defined 
as the basis for the projections for the following three years: 2024, 2025 and 2026. 
Similarly, 32 variables are considered at the macroeconomic level for each of the 
referred scenarios.
Regarding the Solvency Ratio, in the base scenario we comply in all the years of the 
projection with the minimum requirements of Basic Solvency, Additional Basic Solvency 
Ratio and Total Solvency Ratio, taking into account the implementation plan of the 
conservation buffer defined in Decree 1477 of 2018. In the case of the adverse scenario, 
we worked with a hypothetical scenario that would allow us to reach regulatory non-
compliance with the Total Solvency Ratio by 2026. At the beginning of 2026, the Total 
Solvency Ratio was below regulatory levels, a situation that normalized in the mitigating 
scenario and in which it was once again above the aforementioned limits.
As for the CFEN, in the base scenario, the upward behavior of 
the Available Stable Funding (FED) is offset by the increase in 
the Required Stable Funding (RES), which leads to a stability of 
the indicator and its regulatory compliance over the projection 
horizon. In the case of the adverse scenario, there is a non-
compliance with the indicator at the end of 2025 mainly explained 
by the bearish behavior of the Stable Available Funding (FED), 
this situation is reversed in the adverse scenario with mitigating 
factors, based on the Bank’s funding recomposition.
Additionally, and under the guidance received from the supervisor 
under Circular Letter 028 of 2024, the Adverse Climate Risk 
scenario is included through the construction of models that 
allow evaluating the impact of the increase in rainfall on the non-
performing loan portfolio and the portfolio at risk, considering 
the historical behavior from 2019 onwards. This effect was 
incorporated considering the regional segmentation in which 
the bank actively participates, and the initial conditions raised 
in the adverse scenario were taken as a starting point.

The Money Laundering and Terrorist Financing 
Risk Management System (SARLAFT) allows us to 
comply with national and international regulations 
on the prevention of financial crimes, protecting 
its reputation and ensuring that it is not involved in 
illicit activities. Among the functions exercised we 
 C ustomer Due Diligence: It is important for us 
to know our customers through the collection 
and verification of detailed information, such 
as identity, origin of funds, economic activity, 
among others. We do this by assessing risks 
based on the client’s profile, the transactions 
carried out and their geographical location.
 T ransaction Monitoring: We will constantly 
monitor transactions to identify unusual or 
suspicious patterns that may indicate money 
laundering or terrorist financing activities. This 
can include large transactions, international 
transfers, or movements that do not match the 
customer’s profile.
 S uspicious Transaction Reports: When we 
identify a suspicious or attempted transaction, 
we must report it to the Financial Information 
and Analysis Unit – UIAF, which is the competent 
authority in the matter.
 Ongoing T raining: Our employees are regularly 
trained to identify signs of suspicious activity 
and understand the importance of compliance 
with SARLAFT regulations.
 A udit and Evaluation: We conduct internal 
audits to assess the effectiveness of the 
SARLAFT system, ensuring that all procedures 
are in place and regulations are complied with.
 R isk Management: We identify and evaluate 
the risks inherent to our operation, implementing 
measures to mitigate the risks of money 
laundering, terrorist financing and financing 
of the proliferation of weapons of mass 
destruction, this includes the segmentation 
of high-risk customers, the control of specific 
financial products and the implementation of 
additional security measures.

during the second quarter of 2025.

## Página 69
At Banco de Occidente, we reaffirm our commitment to sustainability and the responsible 
management of environmental and social risks through the implementation of the 
Environmental and Social Risk Management System (SARAS). This system was developed 
in 2023 with the support of the NINT consultant, enabling us to define specific parameters 
for  classifying and managing  these risks among ourBusiness Banking clients.
As part of the process, during the second half of 2023, we conducted a pilot test 
involving 30 relationship managers, evaluating all their credit operations. Subsequently, 
on January 31, 2024, we began the phased implementation of SARAS in three phases, 
culminating in July 2024 with 100% coverage of SARAS evaluations for our Business 
Banking customers.
The main objective of SARAS is to identify, mitigate and monitor environmental 
and social risks in the operations evaluated, minimizing the Bank’s exposure 
to regulatory, credit, operational and reputational impacts. The system 
applies to all Business Banking operations, including Business 1 and 2, 
Corporate, Government and the Structured Finance Unit (UFE), across all 
sectors and industries.
Risk Classification and 
SARAS classifies risks into three stages:
We identify prohibited activities and 
activities with exceptions due to their 
environmental and social impact.
We determine the risk category 
Follow-up and Monitoring
We supervise operations with environmental 
and social risk management tools daily.

Integration of ESG Aspects 
into Credit Analysis
From the Structured Finance Unit (UFE), we integrate 
ESG criteria into the analysis of large-scale projects, 
particularly those related to construction sector. We 
evaluate required permits and licenses and engage 
in dialogue with clients to determine if environmental 
and social due diligence is necessary. Before being 
presented to the credit committee, all projects must 
have term sheets reviewed by the UFE team, a project 
engineer. No disbursements are made without the 
required information and the above conditions met.
Evaluation of Operations with 
Environmental and Social Risks
By 2024, we evaluated 60% of the operations served 
by the UFE, including two high-risk cases where an 
environmental and social due diligence report was 
required before proceeding with the evaluation. 
This evaluation is part of the third phase of SARAS 
We have an exclusion list that identifies 
prohibited activities, and we establish 
restrictions for certain activities with 
exceptions, ensuring that they do not exceed 
5% of the Bank’s portfolio.  For high-risk 
transactions, we require environmental and 
social due diligence reportsprepared by 
external experts and reviewed by our senior 
environmental analyst before submission to 
credit approval committees.
Oversight and Accountability 
in ESG Incorporation

Equator Principles
Banco de Occidente is not a signatory to the Equator Principles. However, through SARAS, we assess 
environmental and social risks in Business Banking credit operations, particularly those projects 
managed by the UFE.
Since these projects typically involve high amounts and activities with a higher propensity for 
environmental and social risks, the risk categorization form includes a section to assess the amount 
and phase of the project. If a project is under construction or pre-construction, it is automatically 
classified as high risk.
In 2024, we evaluated 60% of the operations served by the UFE, identifying two high-risk cases 
where an environmental and social due diligence report was requested. We are still in the process 
of reviewing and consolidating information to strengthen our capacity to analyze and mitigate 
environmental and social risks.

At Banco de Occidente, we embed environmental, social, and

Driving the Growth of Our 
Sustainable Portfolio
At Banco de Occidente, we continue to strengthen our 
commitment to sustainability through the financing of 
projects and activities with positive environmental and 
social impact. Based on our sustainable taxonomy, 
we identified that our sustainable portfolio for 
2024 reaches $3.61 trillion, of which $3.43 trillion 
correspond to own portfolio and $173.262 billion 
to development portfolio.
Within our own portfolio, 25%  is allocated to 
environmental initiatives, with an emphasis on 
Green Buildings and Renewable Energy,  while 
75% corresponds to financing with social impact, 
focused on SME owned or managed by Women 
and Affordable Infrastructure. 
In line with our long-term vision, we have set out to 
achieve a sustainable portfolio of $8 trillion by 
2030. With the results obtained in 2024, we have 
advanced 43%[2]  towards our goal, consolidating 
our role as a key player in the development of a 
more sustainable economy.
In addition, we aim to ensure that the share of 
the sustainable portfolio within our total portfolio 
continues to grow year after year. Currently, this 
segment represents 7% of our total portfolio, and 
we continue to drive strategies to expand its reach 
and impact in the coming years.
Sustainable Finance 
Products and Services
At Banco de Occidente, we recognize the critical role 
we play in the transition to a low-carbon economy 
and sustainable development. Through our offer 
of sustainable finance products and services, we 
seek to promote responsible investments, mitigate 
risks associated with unsustainable financing and 
generate value for our clients and society.
Our portfolio of solutions is designed to support 
companies, consumers and SMEs in the adoption 
of more sustainable practices, facilitating access 
to financial resources aligned with environmental 
and social criteria. From credit lines focused on 
energy efficiency and sustainable construction to 
products designed to promote clean mobility and 
social welfare, our strategy integrates sustainability 
as a cross-cutting axis in financing.

## Página 80
At Banco de Occidente we have put all our efforts into strengthening the End to End 
(E2E) digital experience, which has allowed our customers to request and obtain 
product approval in an agile and efficient way. Thanks to this strategy, we have 
managed to digitize products such as Credit Cards, Personal Loans, Savings Accounts 
and CDTs consolidating our commitment to innovation and process optimization.
An important milestone was the integration of the digital flow of Personal Loans 
with the Bank’s traditional system, which eliminated the double filing of data and 
significantly improved operational efficiency, this improvement will be massively 
deployed in 2025 for the commercial team, and in the near future we will extend 
this optimization to Housing and Vehicle products.
We also managed to launch the Digital CDT, allowing our customers to request it 
in a completely self-managed way through our portal, without the need to go to a 
branch, this advance is a milestone in the digitization of banking products and lays 
the foundations for a similar flow in Housing that will be implemented in 2025.
In order to improve the experience of our customers, we have developed more agile 
digital flows, a clear example is the optimization in the approval of Personal Loans, 
which is now reduced to only two screens, making the process simpler for both our 
current and new customers, by 2025, we hope to extend this optimization to Housing, 
Credit Cards and Vehicles.

within Grupo Aval.

our sales to be digital in 2024,

## Página 84
At the Bank we have implemented an information security model aligned with international standards 
ISO27001-2022 and NIST 800-53, which is composed of policies, standards and procedures focused on 
protecting the information of both our customers and the entity. These guidelines are documented, approved 
by our senior management and are carried out within our organization.  We regularly review and update this 
model to ensure that it remains aligned with the Bank’s technological advances, thus ensuring a high level 
of information security and adding value to the commitments we have with our customers, shareholders and 
the community at large. 
In addition, we have an evaluation process in collaboration with the consulting firm Ernest & Young (EY), whose 
objective is to measure our level of maturity and ensure that the implementation of the model is adequate 
To comply with the provisions of our security model, 
we have processes, services and tools designed to 
control cyber risk and we have an incident response 
plan that seeks to mitigate the impact in terms of 
availability, confidentiality and integrity of services, 
in the event of security or cybersecurity incidents.
Regulatory compliance 
and privacy audits 
We rigorously comply with Law 1581 on the Protection 
of Personal Data, guaranteeing that the collection, 
storage and processing of our clients’ personal 
data is carried out in full respect of the principles 
of transparency, legality and security. In compliance 
with the above we carry out periodic audits in terms 
of cybersecurity to evaluate the effectiveness of our 
information leakage prevention (DLP) controls.  
Culture of information 
security and cybersecurity
We ensure that all our employeesare aware of the 
risks and importance of information security and 
cybersecurity, for this, we have implemented policies 
and procedures that allow them to understand and 
face possible threats.
In addition, we carry out mandatory annual training 
through the Success Factors platform, where 
knowledge and good practices on information 
security are reinforced. If any employeedetects 
suspicious activity, we have a clear process to 
report it, detailed in Procedure AVBO-PRSI-SI-002, 
“Security Incident Report”. 
In 2024, we trained 5,667 employees through in 
person talks and reached 5,467 more through the 
virtual course, thus reinforcing our culture of data 
protection and security.
Although information security and cybersecurity are 
not directly included in the performance evaluation, 
we treat each incident with care, working together 
with the Human Talent area to evaluate the impact 
and take the necessary actions, including disciplinary 
measures if necessary.
We implement solid contingency and risk management 
strategies, supported by a specialized team and 
solid governance that involves those responsible 
for security, cybersecurity, business continuity 
and operational risks. In addition, at the time of 
subscribing services, our clients are duly informed 
about the current privacy policies, which reinforces 
our commitment to the protection of their information. 
## Página 85
In addition, we implement continuous awareness campaigns on the main cyber risks 
to mitigate possible threats to information security.  
To address these risks in a comprehensive manner, we have a Security Committee 
that meets monthly, composed of the Vice President of Risks, responsible for the 
areas of Information Security, Operational Risk and Business Continuity, and the Vice 
President of Operations and Technology, Pedro Villegas, who fulfills the role of Chief 
Technology Officer (CTO) and Chief Information Security Officer (CISO). In the same 
way, he is in charge of supervising the Technology Management, which is responsible for 
Cybersecurity in the Bank. At the meetings held, the initiatives in progress are reviewed, 
an exhaustive monitoring of the risks identified and their mitigation is carried out, and 
the incidents that have occurred are evaluated, which ensures robust protection of 
information and operational continuity.  Both Vice-Presidents have extensive previous 
experience related to their responsibility within the financial sector.
IT security, cybersecurity 
processes and infrastructure 
We have established business continuity plans and incident response procedures, 
which are tested at least twice a year Although we do not have certifications such as 
ISO 27001 or NIST, we follow the ISO 27001:2022 framework, evaluated annually by 
E&Y . In addition, we manage vulnerabilities using tools such as Qualys and apply a 
due diligence process with our suppliers to ensure compliance with security standards.
In 2024 we received 4 complaints from regulatory bodies, which is a decrease from the 
7 we received in 2023 and 2022, indicating an improvement in incident management 
through the implementation of more effective internal processes that detect and 
respond quickly to data breaches. This allowed us to contain the impact and reduce 
the number of affected data subjects.

In compliance with the provisions of Law 603 of 2000, Banco de Occidente has defined policies, controls and 
sanctions to guarantee the legality of the software used. The controls for the acquisition, development and 
maintenance of the software, in accordance with the legal requirements on copyright, privacy and electronic 
commerce, are mandatory for compliance by the responsible areas. In this regard, the internal audit carries 
out continuous monitoring to verify adequate compliance with the regulations.
On the other hand, in IT there is a licensing area that manages the SW that has an associated licensing 
and for the SW Free there is a review and approval flow in which IT Architecture and Information Security 
participates through the IT services portal. This review allows these utilities to be included in the bank’s utility 
catalog and facilitates new requests.

employees and contracted third parties; in particular, the following definitions are available in the Information

## Página 87
Standard: Compliance 
with legal regulations and 
external regulations
Any rule, regulation or contractual requirement for 
each computing resource must be explicitly defined 
and formally documented. There must be documents 
that establish how Banco de Occidente’s computer 
resources comply with any internal or external 
regulations, rules or contractual requirements.
Standard: Copyright 
The installation, reproduction, use and storage 
of software, multimedia files and external 
information in the Bank’s computer resources 
must be previously authorized and must comply 
with the legal requirements that enable their use. 
Appropriate procedures should be put in place to 
ensure compliance with legal restrictions on the 
use of material that may be subject to intellectual 
property rights such as copyright and design rights.  
Standard: Installation of 
authorized software
The software that resides in the institution’s computer 
resources may only be authorized by Banco de 
Occidente. Software that is not registered and 
authorized may not be installed or run on Banco 
de Occidente’s computer resources.
Minimum security and 
quality requirements for 
information handling.
Currently, Banco de Occidente can confirm 
compliance with the numerals required by the 
Finance Superintendence of Colombia in the face 
of the latest update of External Circular 029 of 
2019 chapter I “Channels, means, security and 
quality in the management of information in the 
provision of financial services.” It is possible to 
maintain compliance with each of the requirements 
defined therein and in particular with the use of 
biometrics as a differentiating element in the process 
of authenticating the identity of customers and 
users, through the use of the technological solution 
provided by the National Registry of Civil Status and 
Certicamara for this purpose.

Our corporate governance is essential to ensure 
responsible, transparent management aligned with 
the highest national and international standards. In 
2024, we continued to consolidate our governance 
structure with an ethical and sustainable approach, 
implementing new measures such as the creation 
of a Sustainability Committee that oversees our 
ESG practices. In addition, we strengthened 
transparency by publishing annual impact reports 
and implementing independent external audits. With 
these actions, we guaranteed the protection of the 
rights of our shareholders, investors, employees, local 
communities and other stakeholders, reaffirming our 
commitment to an inclusive and responsible model.
In this chapter, we present the practices, policies 
and actions implemented in the field of corporate 
governance, as well as the results obtained, in 
coherence with the principles of transparency, integrity 
and responsibility that guide our management. 
Through this approach, we seek to strengthen our 
position as a solid financial institution, committed to 
the economic and social development of the country, 
while generating long-term sustainable value. 
In 2024 we elaborated the Corporate Governance 
Report for 2023, which seeks to reflect how through 
the implementation of the 148 recommendations of 
the “Country Code” we ensure transparency, ethics 
and accountability in companies. At the Bank we 
achieved an adoption rate of 87.3% (implementation 
of 130 recommendations) which shows our 
commitment to best practices in governance, This 
not only improves the confidence of investors and 
other stakeholders, but also promotes a strong and 
responsible organizational culture.
Our corporate governance is essential 
to ensure responsible, transparent 
management aligned with the highest 
national and international standards.

During the period from January to March 2024, the 
Board of Directors was composed of five (05) main

that modified the structure of the Board, leaving it 
made up for the period from March 2024 to March 
2025 by nine (09) members, without alternates. As 
established in the Bylaws, the deliberative quorum is 
made up of the presence of the majority of Directors.

the Board of Directors:  
 A udit Committee: this committee is in charge 
of generating reports based on transparency 
and detecting opportunities for improvement 
that contribute to the optimization of processes 
and is carried out quarterly.
       It is composed of three (3) members of the Board 
of Directors who have experience, and know, 
among others, accounting, financial and other 
matters associated with the functions assigned 
to the Audit Committee and are independent. 
During the period covered by the report, nine 
(09) sessions were held, of which seven (07) 
were regular and two (02) special.
 C omprehensive Risk Committee: is responsible 
for monitoring the result of the risk profile and 
appetite, advising the Board of Directors on 
operations, events or activities, including the 
incursion into new ones, that may affect the 
entity’s exposure and risk profile, approving 
adjustments and changes to SIAR policies, 
monitoring the state of the risk culture in the 
entity,  evaluating the analysis of the results of 
the monthly risk management reports, among 
others. It is also responsible for promoting the 
adaptation of risk management in society to an 
advanced model that allows the configuration 
of a risk profile in accordance with strategic 
objectives, validating reviews of the positive 
and negative impacts generated by social and 
environmental issues,  supervising compliance 
with the comprehensive management of 
climate change risk and being present in the 
accountability of the SARAS Environmental 
and Social Risk Management System. It is held 
       It is composed of eleven (11) members, of which

 A ppointments, Remuneration and Corporate

of five (5) members appointed by the Board of

Administrative Talent, respectively. Three (03) regular 
sessions were held of this committee.
The inclusion of independent members in committees 
is essential to ensure effective governance and 
impartiality in decision-making, these members, 
having no direct ties to the organization, bring an 
objective and disinterested perspective, which allows 
situations to be evaluated in a more equitable and 
transparent manner. Their independence ensures 
that decisions are made without external influences 
or conflicts of interest, which strengthens internal 
control, fosters shareholder and investor confidence, 
and facilitates compliance with best governance 
practices and regulations. In this way, they contribute 
to the proper functioning of the Bank by protecting 
its long-term interests and promoting ethical and 
## Página 93
appointment process  
The process for appointing the members of the Board 
of Directors was carried out in accordance with the 
provisions of the Bylaws, and was carried out during 
the General Shareholders Assembly on March 20, 
2024. In that Assembly, the electoral quotient system 
was applied, which consists of dividing the number 
of votes obtained by each candidacy by the total 
number of seats available in the constituency, a 
key mechanism for the proportional allocation of 
seats. For the statutory period between March 2024 
and 2025, the Board of Directors was formed in 
accordance with the lists presented by Grupo Aval 
Acciones y Valores S.A., of which seven (07) lines are 
independent, thus ensuring adequate representation 
and balance within the governing body.
Subsequently, the legal procedures to take office were 
carried out before the Finance Superintendence of 
Colombia, which were duly approved.  This process, 
carried out with total transparency, reinforces the 
reliability of the decisions taken and ensures that the 
governance structure is aligned with the country’s 
regulations, providing our shareholders and investors

Changes in the Board of

At the General Shareholders Assembly held on March 
20, 2024, taking into account the list presented by

process considers various aspects relevant to the 
development of the organization. In accordance with 
Article 28 of the bank’s bylaws, it is the responsibility 
of the Shareholders Assembly to freely appoint and 
remove the members of the Board of Directors, 
accept their resignations and fill vacancies. This 
process is carried out after a thorough review by 
the Appointments, Remuneration and Corporate 
Governance Committee, which assesses the suitability 
of the candidates and their independence rating. 
The Board of Directors, or shareholders directly, 
present the proposals to the General Shareholders 
Assembly, ensuring that fundamental aspects such 
as stakeholder opinions, diversity, independence and 
the competencies necessary to address the Bank’s 
impacts are taken into account.

The remuneration system of our Senior Management 
includes a base salary, complemented by an annual 
bonus that is assigned according to the results 
obtained by the Bank in the previous year. This bonus 
is approved directly by Grupo Aval.
On the other hand, Managers who support Senior 
Management receive a full salary. In the case of 
Treasury Management, in addition to this salary, 
an additional quarterly variable compensation is 
offered, which depends on the results achieved 
during that period.
Conflict of interest
We have a Conflicts of Interest Committee (CCI), 
which is responsible for determining, in the process 
of managing situations that may generate a possible 
conflict of interest, whether the operation in question 
is of a regular nature, typical of the ordinary activities 
of the company or is in line with market conditions. 
Otherwise, the Committee will have to decide whether 
to approve or reject the operation.
If, as a result of the analysis of the situation presented, 
the CCI determines that the transaction poses a 
conflict of interest and considers that the decision 
exceeds its scope of competence, it must refer the 
matter to the Board of Directors of the corresponding 
The Board of Directors will evaluate the factors that 
make up the conflict of interest and will make an 
informed decision, in accordance with its legal and 
statutory powers. This decision may be: i) the approval 
of the transaction, ii) the recommendation to refrain 
from carrying it out, iii) the approval subject to certain 
modifications, or iv) the referral of the matter to the 
consideration of the general shareholders assembly. 
The Board will establish the criteria on what type 
of transactions can be decided by itself and which 
must be submitted to the assembly, including, among 
other aspects, materiality criteria.
The policy for identifying, communicating and 
managing conflicts of interest was approved by 
the Board of Directors in Minutes No. 1525 of June 
28, 2019, and we constituted the Conflicts of Interest 
Committee, made up of the following main members: 
financial vice president, risk vice president, legal 
vice president, and alternate members: accounting 
manager, credit risk manager, personal banking 
During the period covered by this report, no conflict of 
interest situations arose that required to be raised to 
the Board of Directors; the other cases were properly 
handled by the Conflicts of Interest Committee.
We also strictly complied with the provisions 
established in its Conflict of Interest Policy, ensuring 
transparency in the management and handling of 
conflicts of interest before its stakeholders. The 
Board of Directors, through its Secretary, keeps a 
detailed record of the operations related to conflicts 
of interest that have been approved, and complies 
with the duty of disclosure established in Decree 
2555 of 2010. This information is included in the 
accountability report that is presented annually to 
the General Shareholders Assembly, which details 
the nature of the situations, the decisions made 
and the corresponding actions. In this context, we 
provide relevant information on aspects such as 
membership of different boards of directors, cross-
shareholding with suppliers and other stakeholders, 
the existence of controlling shareholders, and 
relationships, transactions and outstanding balances 
with related parties. In addition, in our capacity as 
issuer of securities, we inform the general public 
about material conflicts of interest that may arise, 
complying with current Colombian legislation on 
During the period covered 
by this report, no conflict of 
interest situations arose that 
required to be raised to the

information management
We comply with the process of communicating critical 
concerns to the highest governing body, ensuring 
that directors receive the necessary information for 
the development of the Board of Directors sessions 
in a timely manner. With the support of the Board 
Secretary’s task force, relevant documentation and 
reports are distributed in advance, usually a minimum 
of five days prior to the session. Critical concerns 
and information are communicated through digital 
tools such as the Teams platform and email, making it 
easy to access information and be able to efficiently 
address urgent or relevant topics before meetings.
Collective knowledge of the 
highest governing body
During 2024, three (3) members of our Board 
of Directors obtained the ESG Director Training 
Certificate granted by the IFC, which allowed them 
to strengthen their capacities in environmental, social 
and corporate governance.
The evaluation of the Board of Directors is carried 
out from a collegiate perspective, individually and 
by each of the committees that make up the board, 
through questionnaires, this year being for the first 
time a self-evaluation process in a totally digital 
way with the use of the Microsoft Forms tool.  
For the preparation of these 
questionnaires, aspects to be evaluated 
are taken into account, such as the 
structure and conformation, agenda 
and strategic focuses, fulfillment 
of responsibilities, dynamics and 
operability of the board.  
In addition, the board evaluation contemplates a 
weighting of the board’s decisions that direct the 
organization’s actions that influence the economy 
and the lives of our customers through our products 
For the year 2024, the self-assessment of our Board 
reflected an effective governance body, which 
fulfills the main responsibilities of governance and 
is committed to contributing to the development of 
the Bank. The average rating of the development of 
the Bank’s Board of Directors 2024 is 4.78/5.0. It is 
worth highlighting key elements that result in high 
ratings and denote in general a good corporate 
governance system: i. The climate of trust in the 
Board sessions, open communication that facilitates 
discussions, and a constructive approach to making 
better decisions. ii. The autonomy that the members 
of the Board of Directors have, attending to their 
duties as administrators (acting in good faith, with 
loyalty and with the diligence of a good businessman), 
and iii. The good level of trust that the Board of 
Directors has in the Administration, which facilitates 
At the committee level, the Audit and Risk committees

Remuneration and Corporate Governance Committee, 
opportunities for improvement were identified with 
which an improvement plan is being developed to 
be implemented in the coming year.

process of evaluation of the members of the Board

## Página 104
Senior Management evaluation
The members of Senior Management are evaluated 
through the Balance Scorecard (BSC) which is 
measured monthly and whose results reports are 
socialized every 3 months (approximately). The 
Balance Scorecard is measured internally by the 
Financial Planning and Budget Management, under 
the control of figures (updated in accordance with 
the Bank’s goals) and indicators specific to each 
area (which were adopted several years ago as a 
result of an external consultancy). These metrics are 
lowered at the level of leaders of the organization 
under a cascading scheme, seeking alignment 
within management and forming part of their annual 
performance assessment. 
Internal Control System (ICS)
The Internal Control System (ICS) of the Bank and its 
Affiliates is a continuous and dynamic process that 
seeks to improve efficiency in its various elements, 
including the control environment, risk management 
and monitoring, with the active participation of all 
our employees, from the operational levels to the 
Board of Directors. The Internal Audit, independent 
and objective, supervises compliance with the 
governance and control processes under the current 
regulatory framework, executing risk-based audits 
and presenting the results and recommendations to 
the Audit Committee of the Board of Directors on 
a quarterly basis. In addition, it fosters a culture of 
risk management through an annual training plan.
Evaluation of the performance of 
the Internal Control System (ICS)
In compliance with the provisions of the basic legal 
circular of the Finance Superintendence of Colombia, 
our Internal Control System (ICS) and its subsidiaries 
were properly managed during 2024, achieving 
reasonable risk mitigation. This evaluation was based 
on the comprehensive analysis of the components 
of the ICS, including the Control Environment, Risk 
Management, Control Activities, Information and 
Communication, Monitoring, and Independent 
Country Code Survey
This survey is essential for the continuous improvement 
of our corporate governance practices, it allows 
us to evaluate and align our processes with the 
highest standards of transparency, ethics and 
accountability. This assessment helps us identify 
areas for improvement, strengthen internal controls, 
and optimize our management, resulting in greater 
investor confidence, a stronger reputation, and a 
better ability to manage risk.
In 2024, we presented our report on the application 
of the Bank’s best corporate governance practices, 
based on this survey, which evaluates five major areas 
of corporate governance and contains thirty-three 
key measures, with a total of up to one hundred and 
forty-eight recommendations. The transmission of 
the Country Code survey, corresponding to the year 
2024, was carried out in January 2025, in which 
130 measures were adopted, 2 measures do not 
apply to Banco de Occidente and the others are 
under analysis, to verify which of them are viable 
for implementation.
The publication of the answers can be found on our 
website, Information Section for Shareholders and 
Information for shareholders

timely information, provided that the established

and is governed by the internal manual MAN-
CAP-066. Our shareholders can access the 
information through various channels, such as 
email, telephone service and the Bank’s website.

of the policies for shareholders found in Article 7 of 
the Bank’s bylaws, which establish that:
## Página 105
Each share shall entitle one (1) vote in all decisions 
of the General Shareholders Assembly with the 
restriction set forth in Article 22 of these Bylaws. 
The Company will also treat its shareholders in the 
exercise of the right to petition, complaints and 
information, regardless of the value of their shares. 
Among the specific mechanisms that ensure equitable 
treatment of shareholders are: (i) requesting the 
call to the Shareholders Assembly in accordance 
with the provisions of these bylaws and the Code of 
Good Governance, (ii) demanding compliance with 
the Code of Good Governance, (iii) being answered 
and informed in the same detail and at the same 
time and opportunity in order to protect their rights. 
The attention and provision of information to the 
Company’s shareholders will be made through the 
unit that the Company assigns for their attention. (iv) 
the others provided for in these bylaws, in the Code 
of Good Governance and in the Law.

by mitigating risks and avoiding penalties that could 
negatively impact the profitability of managed 
As a Bank, our legal management is aligned 
with compliance with environmental, social and 
governance (ESG) regulations, ensuring responsible 
and sustainable practices in all our operations. In this 
context, the Legal Vice Presidency plays a fundamental 
role in leading the design, implementation and 
supervision of the regulatory policies that govern 
our entity, ensuring compliance with regulations 
on business ethics, human rights and transparency. 
Through the constant monitoring of national and 
international regulations, the updating of internal 
procedures and the training of our employees in 
compliance principles, the Legal Vice Presidency 
strengthens corporate governance and mitigates 
risks associated with regulatory non-compliance, 
regulatory sanctions, fraud, corruption and violations 
of labor and human rights.
Our legal and regulatory management is articulated 
with anti-corruption, regulatory compliance and 
labor rights policies, promoting a culture of integrity 
and reinforcing our commitment to an ethical and 
sustainable operation. This work allows us not only 
to comply with applicable regulations, but also to 
anticipate new regulatory challenges, ensuring 
transparency and the trust of our stakeholders.
We also continued to strengthen our fraud prevention

teams, and strengthening our incident response 
protocols. These actions allow us to reduce 
vulnerabilities and strengthen our clients’ confidence 
in the protection of their financial assets.
## Página 106
Legal and regulatory management structure 
Our Legal Vice-Presidency is in charge of leading regulatory management and 
is made up of three managements: 
 L egal Process and Corporate Governance Management: which is 
responsible for managing legal risk within the framework of operational 
risk, as well as overseeing internal regulatory development and corporate 
governance structure. . 
 J udicial Processes Management: is responsible for managing litigation 
against the bank and has advisors specialized in labor and tax matters. 
 A sset Standardization Management: is the one who manages the recovery 
of specialized portfolio and non-performing loans, standing out for its 
contribution to the generation of the bank’s profits by meeting demanding 
budget goals through its efficient collection management. 
In addition, conciliation is an alternative dispute resolution mechanism that allows 
the parties to reach an agreement without the need to go to court. Through this 
procedure, an agile, effective and mutually beneficial solution is sought, with the 
intervention of a neutral third party that facilitates dialogue and negotiation. In 
our case, this mechanism is key to resolving disputes in a timely manner, avoiding 
lengthy litigation and ensuring a fair response for clients.
Litigation, judicial and 
administrative proceedings
Judicial proceedings against the Bank that represent a material impact are 
adjusted annually, following established accounting and financial standards. 
This adjustment is made based on the bank’s profits and the application of 
accounting principles that determine the provision necessary to cover possible 
contingencies. In this way, at the Bank we recognize and responsibly manage 
the risks associated with these litigations, ensuring that their financial impact is 
duly reflected in the financial statements. 
Therefore, the legal proceedings against the Bank that represent a material 
impact (with claims equal to or greater than $4.061MM) are detailed in notes 23 
and 24 of the Separate and Consolidated Financial Statements, respectively.
We believe that the probability of losses arising from these litigations is low, so 
we do not consider it necessary to make provisions. In addition, we have legal 
risk management mechanisms that allow us to monitor and prevent situations 
that may lead to litigation. At the time of being notified of a process, a report is 
made to the Operational Risk area so that they can manage these risks and are 
able to mitigate them. None of our affiliates presents significant judicial processes 
that require disclosure in this report.
At the Bank we recognize and responsibly manage the risks 
associated with these litigations, ensuring that their financial 
impact is duly reflected in the financial statements.

social fabric and slow down economic growth. 
Likewise, this type of practice can cause a loss of

the assets of our investors, customers and suppliers, 
and generate social repercussions.

understand the importance of being guided by sound

guarantee the detection and effective management of any irregularity.

## Página 110
Our Board of Directors assumes responsibility for 
identifying and understanding corruption-related 
risks, approving the Internal and External Fraud Policy, 
and overseeing its implementation. On a regular basis, 
it receives information on the assessment of these 
risks in a clear, complete and timely manner, with 
defined criteria to promote continuous improvement. 
Under the risk management model, a 3-line 
scheme has been defined, and it is important that 
employees know their functions to know which 
line they belong to.
The first line of defense is responsible for identifying, 
evaluating and managing the risks associated with 
products, activities, processes and systems under its 
direction. It is mainly made up of the business areas, 
those that interact directly with the stakeholders that 
affect operations and those related to the accounting 
record (commercial, administrative, purchasing and 
In our structure, the second line of defense, made 
up of the Risk and Compliance areas, constantly 
supervises compliance with obligations against the 
risk of corruption. These areas collaborate closely 
with the first line, supporting it in the identification 
of risks and qualification of controls to measure the 
effectiveness of the actions implemented, identify 
possible gaps and determine the level of residual 
risk, facilitating the implementation of corrective and 
preventive action plans. In addition, these tasks are 
led by the Vice Presidency of Risk and Collection and, 
in the specific case of corruption, by the Bank Security 
Management, which coordinates investigations 
for violation of policies and supervises corrective 
and disciplinary actions. In this way, we guarantee 
robust management aligned with international best 
practices in terms of transparency and regulatory 
The third line of defense, on the other hand, 
conducts independent evaluations on corruption 
risk management, as well as on related processes 
and systems, reporting to the Audit Committee with 
periodic reports. In addition, independent audits play 
a fundamental role in strengthening the confidence of 
our investors and other stakeholders. These external 
reviews allow us to evaluate the effectiveness of 
our controls, ensuring transparency and alignment 
with international standards. The results and 
recommendations derived from these audits allow 
us to continuously strengthen our governance 
practices, improve risk management, and reinforce 
our commitment to ethics and sustainability.
To ensure the effectiveness of these controls, we 
promote an ethical culture in which all our employees 
participate in training, along with some suppliers 
who act as intermediaries with public entities and 
employees, to strengthen their commitment to the 
principles of transparency.  This year, compliance 
with the annual ABAC virtual course was 98%; in 
addition, the ABAC culture survey was carried out 
for relevant positions, with a completion of 71%.
## Página 111
Under the framework of the Corporate Anti-Corruption and Bribery Policy (ABAC), 
all special operations and Third-Party Intermediaries (TPI) with which we maintain 
business relations were exhaustively evaluated by the risk area, obtaining a 
favorable concept in each of the cases. These evaluation processes not only 
guarantee compliance with our internal policy, but also ensure transparency in 
our management and accountability to our stakeholders. The results of these 
assessments are reported in accordance with these standards, strengthening 
confidence in our due diligence and risk mitigation practices. 
Regarding the significant risks identified through the risk assessment, the ABAC 
policy clearly defines the operations that, due to their characteristics, could 
involve a greater exposure to the materialization of a corruption risk.
Among these operations are donations, sponsorships, contributions to social 
programs under the sustainability model, acceptance and/or delivery of gifts 
and invitations, public or political contributions, and mergers or acquisitions. 
In order to ensure transparency and compliance with the established policies, 
the risk area carried out the implementation of due diligence on 100% of the 
operations carried out by the entity, reaching a total of 412. This figure represents 
a reduction compared to the previous year, when 481 operations were evaluated. 
Finally, it was possible to guarantee that none of the operations represented a 
risk of corruption for the Bank. In addition, all suppliers that, due to the type of 
service provided, were classified as TPI, to identify the level of risk and determine 
the due diligence necessary to mitigate said risk. The number of operations

Culture of Integrity
Within the framework of comprehensive and 
transparent management, we have the Code of Ethics 
and Conduct and the Internal Work Regulations, these 
guidelines, all our employees sign a commitment of 
conduct and compliance at the time of their entry 
and when these documents are updated.
In the event of any situation that may represent a 
breach of the established rules, employees have the 
obligation to report it to their immediate supervisor 
or, as appropriate, to the Vice Presidency of Human 
Talent, the Internal Audit Management, the Compliance 
Management or the Bank Security Management. This 
mechanism strengthens the culture of control and 
risk mitigation, ensuring the confidence of customers, 
shareholders and other stakeholders.
We believe in equality as a 
right and equity as the guiding 
principle of our organizational 
identity. In our labor relations, we 
guarantee an environment free of 
discrimination and, throughout the 
period, we have not recorded cases 
The Bank’s Ethics Hotline is a confidential and 
anonymous channel available for our employees, 
customers, users, suppliers, contractors or any 
individual to report situations related to fraud, 
corruption, bribery, money laundering or other 
irregular activities that compromise the entity’s 
ethical standards.
Its main objective is to prevent, detect and mitigate 
risks arising from improper practices, such as conflicts 
of interest, guaranteeing the confidentiality of the 
information provided and protecting the identity of 
those who make the complaint.
Types of reports that can be handled through the 
Ethics Hotline include:
 T he improper use or misappropriation of the 
 A cts contrary to the values and principles 
established in the Codes of Ethics, Conduct 
and Good Governance
 Violatio n of internal rules or policies.
 Imp roper disclosure of confidential information. 
The Ethics Hotline is designed to promote 
compliance with ethical standards and prevent 
fraud or malpractice. All complaints received 
are investigated and, once the analysis is 
completed, they are submitted to the Audit 
Committee. In addition, twice a year, a report 
is prepared with the number of complaints 
received and their treatment.
The administration of the channel is led by the 
Internal Audit Management, which guarantees 
the confidentiality of the reports and manages 
the channel of the Ethics Hotline. This channel is 
available both on our web portal and on the Grupo 
Aval portal, facilitating access to the community in 
general. Its existence and operation are disclosed 
every six months by email to customers, suppliers 
and employees, in addition to being published on 
Once a complaint is received, the Internal Audit 
Management performs an initial analysis and 
directs the reports to the corresponding areas, 
establishing a reasonable period for the follow-up 
and communication of the results. In complex cases, 
external specialists, such as forensic auditing, can 
be called upon to conduct a more in-depth analysis. 
If irregularities are identified, the areas involved, 
such as the Labor Relations Management, manage 
the cases and apply the corresponding sanctions 
in accordance with the bank’s policies.
It is the responsibility of the Internal Audit not only to 
investigate the reported cases, but also to follow up 
on the reported situations and analyze their causes 
to strengthen the ethical culture and continuously 
improve internal processes.

## Página 122
At Banco de Occidente, sustainability is an essential 
part of our management. From the Sustainability 
Management, we work in coordination with the 
different areas of the bank to integrate environmental, 
social and governance criteria into our operations, 
ensuring that each decision has a positive impact 
on the environment, on our customers and on the 
communities where we operate.
Our sustainability strategy is based on the creation 
of long-term value for our stakeholders, promoting a 
balance between economic growth, environmental 
management and social well-being. We take a 
comprehensive approach that allows us to mitigate 
risks and seize sustainability opportunities, ensuring 
a responsible and resilient operation in the face of 
global challenges.
Our strategy is aligned with the Global Pact and the 
Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs), as well 
as with good practices of the Asobancaria Green 
Protocol and Principles for Responsible Banking 
(PBR). This has allowed us to consolidate efforts 
consistent with international trends and advance in 
our commitments to sustainable development.
In 2024, we participated for the second time in S&P 
Global’s annual corporate sustainability assessment 
(CSA), achieving 48 points, which represents an 
advance of 6 points compared to the previous year 
and positions us in the 79th percentile* globally in the 
banking industry. This result allows us to measure our 
performance against more than 660 companies in 
the sector, identify our strengths and draw a roadmap 
to continue moving forward.
Thanks to the joint work of the teams and the 
support of the leaders of the different areas, we 
have strengthened our management of ESG criteria, 
consolidating a solid strategy with clear goals. 
Our goal is to continue climbing positions in this 
evaluation and continue to advance towards the 
goal of being one of the most sustainable banks 
*These results correspond to January 2025.
Sustainability management is based on key policies 
and ongoing dialogue with our stakeholders. Our 
strategy includes a participatory approach to identify 
expectations, prioritize key issues, and build trusting 
relationships with all relevant stakeholders. To this 
end, we have integrated ESG principles into our 
operations, financial products and strategic decision-
making, which allows us to better serve the needs 
of our clients and contribute to the development of 
a more resilient and equitable financial system. In 
addition, we adopt responsible business conduct, 
integrating environmental and social criteria into our 
business activities and throughout our supply chain.  
Our sustainability strategy 
is based on the creation 
of long-term value 
for our stakeholders,

## Página 124
At Banco de Occidente, the materiality determination 
process is carried out every two years, and is based 
on an exhaustive analysis of the most relevant issues 
from both an internal and external perspective. 
This exercise is conducted in alignment with GRI 
reporting frameworks and Dow Jones Sustainability 
Index requirements, considering the most significant 
economic, social, and environmental impacts for 
the organization and its stakeholders.
Our materiality process involves the active 
participation of external stakeholders, who are 
invited to contribute to the identification and 
prioritization of material issues. This engagement 
includes consultations with groups such as 
customers, regulators, suppliers, communities and 
others, allowing us to take a broad view of the 
expectations and concerns that affect us as a bank 
and the environment in which we operate. Through 
this exercise, we ensure that material topics not only 
reflect the needs of the business, but also those of 
external stakeholders.
Material issues are prioritized through a materiality 
matrix, which is used to evaluate both the impact of 
the different issues on internal operation and their 
impact on society and the environment. The matrix 
considers the risks and opportunities associated with 
each topic, allowing the identification of strategic 
priorities in the short, medium and long term.
In addition, the materiality assessment is fully 
integrated into our risk management (ERM) process. 
This integration is key to ensuring that material 
risks and opportunities are addressed within 
the institution’s overall risk management and to 
maintaining continuous alignment between our 
business strategy and sustainability requirements.
The evaluation process is externally verified, which 
provides transparency and reliability to the results. 
Subsequently, the results of the materiality analysis 
are presented to the Board of Directors, who review 
and approve the strategic priorities derived from this 
exercise. This approach ensures that the bank’s key 
decisions are informed by the material issues most 
relevant to our sustainability and long-term value 
The information related to this process, as well as 
the results of the materiality analysis, are publicly 
available in our management and sustainability 
business continuity. The second perspective, impact 
(from the inside out), exhaustively evaluated the actual 
and potential material impacts, both positive and 
negative, that our operations and portfolio generate 
on the environment and on our stakeholders.
This analysis was carried out in compliance with 
the requirements of the Finance Superintendence 
of Colombia through circulars 031 of 2021 and 012 
of 2022, as well as the new requirements of GRI. 
Dual materiality analysis is a strategic tool that 
allows us to identify and assess issues that influence 
economic, social and environmental value creation. 
Its purpose is to comprehensively address the 
impacts on the environment and the expectations 
of our various stakeholders, in addition to managing 
risks and impacts related to ESG aspects, which 
could have financial implications with an impact 
on business continuity. This exercise was based on 
the scientific method, the ISO 31000 standard, and 
the methodologies of EFRAG, SASB, TCFD and GRI 
reports, thus ensuring compliance with international 
standards and our transparency towards stakeholders.
In line with our purpose of making the development 
transformation of the country a reality, we carried 
out a process of review and updating of our material 
affairs, in collaboration with the consulting firm 
Bufete para el Desarrollo Sostenible (BDS Group).
This exercise was developed following the Double 
Materiality model, which addressed two key 
perspectives. The first, from the financial approach 
(from the outside in), aimed at identifying the current 
and future risks that ESG issues generate in our 
financial situation, development, performance and 
position. These factors can influence our value and

## Página 127
Impact Materiality
Impact materiality aims to evaluate and understand 
the effects that our activities generate on the 
environment, considering both positive and negative 
impacts. This process involved a thorough diagnosis 
of how our operations affect the environment, natural 
resources, climate change, human rights, and social 
well-being. The impact criteria considered were:
Favorable: positive impacts that generate tangible 
and measurable benefits, such as reducing 
emissions or promoting gender equality.
Unfavorable: negative impacts, such as pollution 
or human rights violations.
Once assessed, we assign a level of relevance to 
each issue, taking into account the magnitude, scope, 
and probability of occurrence of the impacts, as 
well as the ability to remediate them.  
We identify and prioritize key stakeholders, based 
on their influence and the impact they have on 
our operations. We then conducted a survey to 
learn about their concerns and perceptions of the 
ESG issues most relevant to the bank. The priority 
stakeholders were the following:
Senior Management.
Board of Directors.
Through this process, we determined which ESG 
issues are priorities for the bank and its environment. 
The outcome of the consultation, together with the 
internal diagnoses, allowed us to define a clear vision 
on the impacts and how to address them effectively.
Financial Materiality
At Banco de Occidente, financial materiality aims 
to identify and evaluate ESG issues that may have 
a significant impact on our financial condition, 
operating performance and compliance with our 
corporate strategy.
To carry out this assessment, we start by identifying 
ESG issues relevant to our industry. We analyze the 
possible risks and impacts associated with each of 
these issues and their relationship with the business.
Once the risks and impacts associated with ESG 
matters were identified, we conducted a detailed 
assessment involving 9 members of our Senior 
Management, 5 representatives of the Board of 
Directors and 14 heads of the risk and strategy areas. 
In addition, we have the assessment of BDS Group, 
who analyzed and rated ESG matters according to 
their relevance and their potential impact on Banco 
de Occidente’s financial and operational stability.
This process included the analysis of: type of 
risk, magnitude, scope of impact, probability of 
occurrence, remediability, and impact on our strategic 
The result of this assessment allowed us to identify 
ESG issues that represent a significant financial risk, 
making it easier to make informed strategic decisions 
and take action to address those risks.
## Página 128
Material Issues for Business Value Creation
At Banco de Occidente, our materiality analysis has identified the three key material issues that have a significant impact on the business, which we consider to 
be determinants for long-term value creation. These issues not only directly impact our strategy and operations, but are also critical factors in ensuring the bank’s 
sustainability and growth going forward. Below, we detail these three material topics:
Material Topic 1 Material Topic 2 Material Topic 3
Climate Risk Management: Climate change is a critical issue that affects 
our long-term performance due to increasing regulation on sustainability 
and the demand for green financial products. The transition to a low-carbon 
economy represents both a risk and a significant opportunity for our bank. 
Managing this risk is essential to mitigate impacts on our credit portfolio 
and ensure compliance with international regulations.
Human Development: talent management is crucial to maintain our 
competitiveness and capacity for innovation. Investing in the training 
and development of our employees has a direct impact on our 
operational efficiency and our ability to better serve our customers. 
In addition, aligning our talent strategies with sustainability and 
employeese well-being also reinforces our reputation and social 
Technology and digital transformation: digitalization and the 
incorporation of advanced technologies are essential to improve 
the efficiency of our services and access new markets. Offering 
sustainable financial products through digital platforms not only 
meets customer expectations, but also positions us as a leader 
in financial innovation and allows us to reduce operating costs 
The transition to a low-carbon economy involves a number of opportunities, 
such as financing sustainable projects and attracting customers interested in 
green products. However, it also presents operational risks due to increasingly 
stringent regulations and the potential obsolescence of unsustainable 
assets. Managing these risks allows us to reduce costs associated with 
non-compliance with regulations and position ourselves in the market as 
a responsible and sustainable entity.
Human talent is the engine of our innovation and growth. Investing 
in development and training programs can improve operational 
efficiency, reduce employeese turnover and increase customer 
satisfaction. In addition, a skilled team is critical to implement 
our sustainable strategies and adapt our products and services 
to the needs of a changing market. This translates directly into an 
increase in profitability and operational efficiency.
Digitalization allows us to offer more accessible, efficient and 
sustainable financial products, reducing operating costs and 
improving customer satisfaction. Through sustainable financing, we 
not only respond to the expectations of investors and regulators, 
but also open up new revenue streams. In addition, the integration 
of emerging technologies into our product offering strengthens 
our competitiveness in the long term, ensuring our relevance in 
Integrating sustainability and climate risk management into our business 
strategy not only reduces financial risks related to climate change, but also 
strengthens our reputation as a responsible entity, generating value both in 
terms of revenue and stakeholder satisfaction. This approach contributes 
to the bank's long-term stability.
The impact of this strategy is wide-ranging, as well-trained and 
engaged staff translates into higher performance, lower turnover, 
and a better relationship with customers. In addition, this contributes 
to a better corporate image and reputation.
The implementation of advanced technologies not only optimizes 
our internal processes, but also allows us to serve a broader 
market with innovative solutions, creating a constant stream of 
value for our clients and for the institution.
We are implementing a comprehensive strategy to decarbonize our operations 
and financing. This includes financing green projects, integrating environmental 
criteria into our credit decisions, and aligning with international climate 
change regulations. In addition, we have set long-term emission reduction 
targets, which drives our investment decisions and ensures the sustainability 
of our operations. In parallel, we integrate climate risk assessment into our 
risk management system (ERM) to ensure that our decisions are aligned 
with sustainability goals and regulatory compliance.
We have launched initiatives to strengthen the development of our 
employees, including leadership programs, well-being and training 
in various topics. In addition, we are implementing inclusion and 
diversity policies to improve staff satisfaction and engagement. 
These strategies are aligned with our vision to be an innovative and 
socially responsible company, which reinforces our organizational 
culture and improves long-term performance.
Our digital strategy focuses on modernizing our banking services, 
providing digital access platforms for sustainable financial 
products, such as green loans. We are also investing in emerging 
technologies, such as artificial intelligence and data analytics, 
to optimize our operations and deliver personalized customer 
experiences. These initiatives allow us to be leaders in the 
sustainable financial sector and stay competitive in a digitalized

Carbon Emissions and Climate Change (Environmental Impact)
Financial Inclusion and Access to Financial Services for Women-Led 
SMEs (Social Impact)
Financing and investment activities in infrastructure and energy 
projects contribute to greenhouse gas emissions, particularly those 
related to the energy sector and construction. This cause is mainly 
associated with the financing of projects that are not sustainable in 
terms of carbon emissions, which is a central aspect of our materiality 
assessment in the environmental context.
The lack of access to financial services, especially in the case of 
women entrepreneurs and businesswomen in small and medium-
sized enterprises (SMEs), generates economic exclusion that limits 
development opportunities. Women, particularly those who lead 
businesses, face barriers of an economic nature: SMEs led by women 
tend to have less access to capital due to a lack of credit history. 
Social: Women often face difficulties in accessing financial services 
due to prejudice and the lack of a supportive environment that favors 
female entrepreneurship. Infrastructure: Poor financial infrastructure 
can hinder the availability of products tailored to the specific needs 
of women-led SMEs, limiting their ability to formalize or expand their 
External stakeholders/ 
Customers, local communities, governments and society in general, 
as well as the environment. Customers, small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs)
topic for external 
The impact of carbon emissions is significant for external stakeholders 
due to its contribution to global climate change and its effects 
on health, biodiversity, and vulnerable communities. This issue is 
closely linked to long-term sustainability and affects the company's 
reputation, as well as relationships with regulators and customers 
who demand more sustainable products and services. 
For SMEs led by women, the lack of access to adequate financial 
products not only affects individual economic stability, but also 
restricts the growth of these companies, preventing their expansion 
and generating a significant gap compared to companies led by men. 
This situation has a direct impact on local economic development, 
as women represent a key source of innovation and employment.

## Página 133
At Banco de Occidente, we are actively committed to sustainability 
and the transition to a low-carbon economy. Through our climate 
strategy, we integrate environmental considerations into our decisions, 
promote impact reduction, and strengthen our capacity to adapt. In 
this section, we present our approach and key actions to contribute 
to a more sustainable future.
We recognize that climate change is a global challenge 
that demands immediate action. For this reason, 
we integrate climate criteria into our strategy and 
risk management, promoting sustainable financing 
and strengthening our capacities in disclosure and 
transparency. For more details on our approach 
and progress, we invite you to consult Annex 3 of 
Financed emissions
We are committed to sustainability and responsible 
management of our environmental impact. As 
a financial institution, we understand that our 
contribution to the transition to a low-carbon 
economy lies not only in our own operations, but 
also in the environmental impact of the sectors and 
projects we finance.
For this reason, in 2024 we carried out our first 
measurement of financed emissions, a key exercise 
for understanding and managing our indirect carbon 
footprint. This assessment was carried out based on 
our 2023 portfolio, prioritizing three strategic sectors: 
Oil & Gas, Construction and Power Generation. 
The selection of these sectors responded to their 
significant impact on the environment, the amount 
of emissions generated in their operations and the 
availability of information.
Contents AnnexesGovernance 
## Página 134
To carry out this measurement, we adopted the 
methodology developed by the Partnership for 
Carbon Accounting Financials (PCAF) and used 
the tool provided by the Sustainable Banking 
Alliance (ABS) in Colombia, supported by USAID 
and Asobancaria. This methodology allowed us to 
quantify the absolute scope 1, 2 and 3 emissions of 
the prioritized sectors, considering the balances of 
our 2023 portfolio.
In this first measurement, the data was broken 
down by asset class (corporate loans and Project 
Finance), sector/industry (Oil & Gas, Construction 
and Power Generation), segment (Large Corporate 
and Business Banking customers) and country/
region (Colombia - 100%). This initial analysis is a 
fundamental starting point and we will include new 
sectors in the calculation annually to have a more 
comprehensive view of our carbon footprint.
While we don´t currently have specific reduction 
targets or net-zero targets, this measurement marks 
the beginning of a structured path to understanding 
the carbon footprint of our funded operations. Based 
on these results, we will work on the formulation 
of strategies and action plans that will allow us 
to support our clients in the transition to more 
sustainable business models.
Additionally, as part of our commitment to 
sustainability, we have internal policies that establish 
guidelines to mitigate environmental impacts in 
our financing operations. Our Sustainable Finance 
Guidelines, the Environmental and Climate Change 
Policy and the Environmental and Social Risk 
Management System (SARAS) Policies are key tools 
in this process. These policies allow us to identify 
clients with high environmental impacts, sectors 
vulnerable to climate change, and opportunities 
to foster sustainable investments through our 
Sustainable and Transition Taxonomy.
The Bank’s senior management plays a key role in this 
commitment. In 2022, we created the Sustainability 
Committee, which is responsible for making strategic 
decisions on environmental, social and governance 
(ESG) matters. This committee oversees, among other 
aspects, the management of our financed emissions 
and allows us to consolidate a comprehensive 
strategy to align our operations with the global 
decarbonization agenda.
We know that addressing the challenge of financed 
emissions requires joint efforts, which is why we 
actively participate in collaborative initiatives with 
other financial institutions and industry associations. 
Our participation in the Sustainable Banking 
Alliance (ABS) in Colombia has allowed us to access 
standardized tools and methodologies to improve 
the measurement of our emissions and work hand 
in hand with other actors in the implementation of 
best practices in the industry.
This is just the first step on a path that will allow us to 
more effectively manage our indirect environmental 
impact. As we move forward in this process, we 
will continue to strengthen our capacities, explore 
new opportunities for sustainable financing, and 
develop strategies that allow us to reduce financed 
emissions, thus contributing to the construction of 
a more sustainable and resilient economy.

Emissions Management – Carbon Footprint
As part of our eco-efficiency goals, we committed to reducing direct emissions in our scopes 1 and 2 by 42% 
by 2030, in line with the scientific goals of limiting global warming to 1.5°C.  We continue to review the process 
for the presentation and validation of reduction targets before the SBTi initiative in the medium term, which 
is why we have participated in webinars, talks given by external parties (Global Compact and Asobancaria) 
to obtain a greater understanding of the process and the activities involved.
We established as our baseline the emissions generated during 2022 due to the stability of the data obtained 
for that period. The emissions generated and the reduction achieved are detailed below:
The calculation of our emissions is under the GHG Protocol standard with a focus on consolidation of 
operational control and, due to the emission sources identified, CO2, CH4, N2O, SF6, HCFs and HCFCs are 
included in the calculation. 
On the other hand, biogenic emissions are presented with a variation that is due to fuel consumption in fixed 
and mobile sources. Specifically, we had an increase in fuel consumption in power plants that was offset by 
the decrease in fuel consumption by vehicles:

We achieved a reduction in our scope 1 
emissions mainly explained by decreases

At Banco de Occidente, we promote the efficient 
and responsible use of resources as part of our 
sustainable vision. We implement actions to optimize 
energy and water consumption, properly manage 
waste and strengthen our environmental criteria in the 
relationship with suppliers. In this section, we share 
our initiatives and progress to minimize our impact 
and contribute to a more sustainable operation.
On the other hand, we manage our energy 
consumption responsibly, aligning ourselves with 
our eco-efficiency goals and the transition to a 
more sustainable model. We implement strategies 
to reduce electricity consumption, optimize the use 
of renewable sources and minimize dependence on 
non-renewable sources. Through energy efficiency 
projects and technological improvements, we make 
progress in reducing our environmental footprint 
and contribute to the fulfilment of our 2030 Agenda.
By 2030, we have set a goal of reducing our electricity 
consumption by 20%, taking 2022 as a baseline. To 
achieve this goal, we are constantly working on the 
implementation of eco-efficiency initiatives that 
allow us to reduce our consumption by at least 2.5% 
reduction of energy consumption was reflected in 2024, evidencing a significant decrease. As a result of these 
initiatives, we achieved a 4.9% reduction in energy consumption from the previous year and a cumulative 
reduction of 11.7% compared to our 2022 baseline.
This progress reflects our commitment to operational efficiency and sustainability, aligning ourselves with 
our eco-efficiency strategy and transition to a more responsible energy model.
At Banco de Occidente, we promote the transition to a more sustainable operation through the use of renewable 
energy sources. In 2024, our six offices with solar panel systems operated throughout the year, reflecting a 
3.1% reduction in the renewable energy consumption indicator. This value will continue to evolve as we move 
forward with the installation of more photovoltaic systems in our offices and headquarters.
Our energy consumption from non-renewable sources comes mainly from the fuel used in the organization’s 
power plants and own vehicles. Aware of the importance of reducing our environmental footprint, since 2022 
we have implemented a vehicle leasing (renting) scheme, allowing us to optimize the use of our fleet and 
significantly reduce fuel consumption. Thanks to this strategy, in 2024 we achieved a 36.01% decrease in 
energy consumption, compared to the previous year.
We maintained our commitment to operational efficiency, using only three Bank fleets, which is two fewer than 
in 2023. However, during this period there was an increase in fuel consumption, due to the need to perform 
preventive maintenance in a greater number of power plants in different areas of the country.

Water is a fundamental resource for our operations, 
and at Banco de Occidente we are committed to 
its responsible and efficient use. We implement 
strategies for the optimization of consumption, the 
reduction of waste and the adoption of technologies 
that allow us to minimize our environmental impact. 
Through these actions, we seek to strengthen our 
eco-efficiency and contribute to the preservation 
of this vital resource.
In our facilities, water is supplied by local aqueduct 
companies in each municipality and city where we 
operate, being used exclusively for domestic uses such 
as sanitation, cleaning and food. As for discharges, 
these correspond to domestic wastewater, which 
is treated and disposed of through the sewerage 
systems of each city, in compliance with current 
environmental regulations.
