Responsible waste management is a priority in our 
commitment to sustainability. We implemented 
strategies focused on the reduction, reuse and 
proper disposal of the waste generated in our 
operations, aligned with our Eco-efficiency Plan 
and the principles of circular economy.
Through segregation at source, process optimization 
and raising awareness among our employees, we 
seek to minimize our environmental impact and 
contribute to meeting the objectives of the 2030 
Within the framework of our Integrated Waste 
Management Plan (PGIR), we worked to identify 
and implement alternatives that allow us to 
minimize the generation of hazardous and non-
hazardous waste in all our activities and processes. 
The waste generated is managed responsibly 
through an authorized environmental manager,  
who is responsible for its proper disposal or use, in 
compliance with current legal regulations.
As part of our strategy, we held awareness sessions 
aimed at all our employees, with the purpose of 
promoting responsible practices that reduce and 
mitigate the environmental impacts associated 
with waste generation. These sessions focus on 
the four main pillars of the PGIR: prevention and 
minimization, internal waste management, external 
waste management, and monitoring and evaluation 
In line with our Eco-efficiency Plan and the 2030 
Agenda, we have set ourselves the goal of gradually 
reducing the waste generated by 20% by 2030, 
reaffirming our commitment to sustainability and 
responsible resource management.
By 2024, we managed to reduce the amount of non-hazardous waste destined for disposal in landfills. This 
waste, although common, special or ordinary, cannot be used due to its characteristics.
On the other hand, we increased the amount of usable waste, especially paper, metal, wood and cardboard, 
as a result of the remodeling processes in our offices and buildings. In addition, we strengthened reduction 
actions, such as the digitization of documents to minimize the use of paper and the promotion of remote 
work to reduce waste generation.
As for hazardous waste, in 2024 there was a considerable increase due to the disposal of construction and 
demolition waste, as well as other usable materials, such as metal, cardboard, wood and paper, within the 
framework of the remodeling carried out in our facilities.

## Página 145
Strategies for the Protection and 
Restoration of Ecosystems
At Banco de Occidente we recognize ecological restoration with native species as 
a fundamental strategy for the conservation and recovery of natural ecosystems. 
Through this practice, we contribute to mitigating environmental degradation, 
biodiversity loss, and the effects of climate change. The use of native plants in these 
processes allows us to improve the functionality of local ecosystems, optimize soil 
quality, strengthen pollination, and expand the availability of habitats for wildlife.
Native species, being adapted to their environment, are more resilient to 
environmental disturbances and play a key role in the stability of ecosystems. 
Their incorporation into ecological restoration projects not only represents an 
investment in the health of the planet and the well-being of future generations, 
but also allows us to preserve biodiversity and guarantee the natural balance 
As part of our commitment to sustainability and climate action, in 2022 we 
established a partnership with the World Wide Fund for Nature (WWF Colombia). 
Through this initiative, we seek to conserve strategic ecosystems within the 
National System of Protected Areas of Colombia (SINAP), promoting active 
restoration processes in collaboration with local communities that have 
decided to transform their practices and contribute to the preservation of the 
Since the beginning of the alliance 
we have managed to plant more than 
17 thousand seedlings nationwide.
In the third year of the Community Restoration initiative in Colombia, we have 
made significant progress in the recovery of ecosystems and the strengthening 
of communities in various regions of the country. These achievements have 
been made possible by our commitment and continued support as a strategic 
ally and key partner since the inception of this collaboration in 2022.
At Banco de Occidente we have played a key role in the financing and execution 
of essential activities within the conservation and restoration program. Our 
contribution has allowed the implementation of projects in strategic protected 
areas, promoting not only environmental regeneration, but also the economic 
and social development of local communities.
## Página 146
Through this alliance, we have provided financial 
resources, training and access to visibility platforms, 
thus strengthening the impact of the actions carried 
In this third year of implementation, we have made 
significant progress in ecosystem restoration 
in four key regions within Colombia’s National 
System of Protected Areas (SINAP). In addition, we 
have promoted the social appreciation of nature 
through citizen participation and the mobilization 
of our employees, reaffirming our commitment to 
sustainability and environmental protection.

Farallones de Cali 
National Natural Park
The Farallones de Cali National Natural Park is the 
largest continental protected area of the Pacific SIRAP , 
with a great diversity of climates and ecosystems 
that make it an important provider of goods and 
services for the Valle del Cauca community. About 
95% of its territory maintains areas of secondary 
forest and, in some cases, primary forests. These 
natural covers represent important carbon reservoirs 
that contribute to the processes of mitigation and 
adaptation to climate change.
Within the framework of Agreement C185 between 
WWF Colombia and Banco de Occidente, we defined 
the Farallones NNP as one of the four prioritized 
areas to develop restoration processes. During the 
first two years of the initiative, we managed to plant 
more than 5,000 trees and, for the third year (2024-
2025 period), we are making progress in planting an 
additional 2,500 seedlings. In addition to planting, 
these actions include maintenance and replanting, 
thus guaranteeing the impact and sustainability of 
ecological restoration.
This strategy allows the active participation of 
the owners of the land, their families and the local 
community, who with their knowledge of the territory 
identify the areas that require greater intervention and 
the most appropriate species for each ecosystem. 
Their experience with native flora is key in the recovery of degraded landscapes and in the consolidation of 
more resilient ecosystems.
Currently, restoration includes fruit and forage species, strengthening sustainable conservation models 
through tools such as agroforestry. This methodology not only provides environmental benefits, such as 
attracting seed-dispersing fauna and promoting passive restoration, but also generates economic benefits 
for the families involved through the hiring of labor and the purchase of plant material, thus contributing to 
local development and the protection of these strategic ecosystems.

DRMI La Playona and Loma 
La Caleta - Acandí (Chocó)
A Regional Integrated Management District (DRMI) 
is an area where landscapes and ecosystems retain 
their function and composition, despite modifications 
in their structure. These spaces allow communities 
to access their natural and cultural values for 
sustainable use, preservation, restoration, knowledge 
The community forest restoration project “Recovering 
the mountain of the Vidal ravine” is being developed 
within the DRMI La Playona and Loma La Caleta, 
in the Local Council of Furutungo, COCOMASUR 
territory. Its main focus is the recovery of the Vidal 
stream, a tributary of approximately 1,500 to 2,000 
meters in length that begins in the Loma La Caleta 
and flows into the wetlands of La Playona.
This area covers 9,364 hectares, located in the 
north of Chocó, in the northwest end of the Gulf of 
Urabá and southeast of the municipality of Acandí. 
It includes the coastal area of La Playona, the 
mountainous corridor of Loma La Caleta and the 
valley on the right bank of the Tolo River.
Within the framework of an agreement with Banco de 
Occidente, WWF Colombia established an alliance 
with the Community Council of Black Communities 
of the Tolo River Basin and the Southern Coastal 
Zone (COCOMASUR) to develop the project “Recover 
the mountain of the Vidal ravine. Community 
restoration in the DRMI La Playona and Loma La 
Caleta”. This report presents the activities carried out 
between 2023 and 2024, focused on improving the 
state of the riparian vegetation of the Vidal stream, 
a tributary of the La Playona wetland.
The restoration process included: consolidation of a 
community nursery, planting of more than 7,500 native 
trees and monitoring of vegetation to strengthen 
Unlike other projects in the country, this agreement 
contemplated the planting of the 7 ,500 seedlings 
in a single year, without dividing it into phases. The 
execution began in 2023 and concluded in 2024, 
with the following progress: 2,500 seedlings in 2023 
and 5,000 seedlings in 2024.

The forest restoration of the Vidal creek has begun to 
generate favorable conditions for the sustainability 
of the La Playona wetland, a key ecosystem that is 
home to a great diversity of species of fauna and 
flora. This recovery contributes to the water balance 
of several rivers and streams, which are essential for 
the regulation of the water cycle, flood mitigation and 
the sustenance of essential activities such as fishing, 
livestock, agriculture, the use of forest products and 
the sustainable use of wild resources.
In addition, this restoration strengthens the availability 
and quality of water for nearby communities, ensuring 
their access to this vital resource.
High Andean Forest: buffer 
zone of the Chingaza NNP
According to the National Natural Parks website, 
the Chingaza National Natural Park (NNP) is a 
natural and cultural treasure of central Colombia. Its 
mountains hold the secrets and knowledge inherited 
from the Muiscas and Guayupes, indigenous peoples 
who protected this territory, as well as from peasant 
communities that inhabited it until less than 40 years 
Today, Chingaza is a refuge of biodiversity, where 
the ecosystems of high Andean and sub-Andean 
forests and moors are home to a great wealth of 
fauna and flora, revealing the balance of life. Located 
in the eastern Andes mountain range, northeast of 
Bogota, the park extends through 11 municipalities: 
seven in Cundinamarca  (Fomeque, Choachi, La 
Calera, Guasca, Junín, Gachalá and Medina) and 
four in Meta (San Juanito, El Calvario, Restrepo and 
In our commitment to conservation, the Chingaza NNP 
Management Plan establishes two key objectives, 
which guide us in the protection of the area and its 
ecological connectivity with the region:
1. G uarantee the continuity of the Andean-
Orinoco ecosystems, protecting the habitat 
of fauna and flora and ensuring the supply of 
their ecosystem services.
2. Imp rove the ecological connectivity of the 
park’s water sources, ensuring their role in 
the provision, regulation and maintenance of 
environmental services.
To advance these ecological restoration processes, 
in 2022 we established a Collaboration Agreement 
between Grupo Conserva and WWF, with the aim of 
strengthening the regeneration of the high Andean 
forest in the park’s buffer zone. As part of this 
agreement, we acquired, planted and maintained 
2,500 seedlings of native species, planted in the 
Mundo Nuevo sector and cared for two years.
Given the climate and biophysical characteristics of 
the high Andean forest, we carry out the restoration 
with carefully selected native species. The seeds 
used in the production of the plant material came 
from field collection, carried out by the nursery group 
of Chingaza, thus ensuring their adaptation and 
resilience in the ecosystem.

## Página 149
NNP Via Parque Isla 
The Via Parque Isla Salamanca (VIPIS) is a 
Protected Area of the National Natural Parks 
System of Colombia, declared in 1964 with a strict 
conservation approach. It is located in the Ciénaga 
Grande de Santa Marta Lagoon Complex, in the 
department of Magdalena, within the jurisdiction 
of Sitionuevo and Pueblo Viejo, being one of the 
most important natural treasures of the Caribbean 
This protected territory covers approximately 56,200 
hectares, with a diversity of ecosystems including 
mangroves, wetlands, forests and beaches. Its 
ecological value lies in its role as a refuge for a wide 
variety of species, including migratory birds, fish, 
mammals and reptiles.
Given its biological importance and the diversity 
of habitats it hosts, VIPIS has received multiple 
international recognitions. It has been designated 
as an Area of Importance for the Conservation 
of Birds (AICA) and, together with the Fauna and 
Flora Sanctuary of the Ciénaga Grande de Santa 
Marta, was declared in 1998 as a Ramsar Site and 
in 2000 as a Biosphere Reserve by UNESCO.
For the period 2024-2025, we are developing the 
third phase of the restoration project in VIPIS, under 
the agreement “Restoration Process Year 3: Banco 
de Occidente – Protected Area Via Parque Isla 
Salamanca”, in alliance with the Association of 
Users of the Clarín Channel. Through this agreement, 
we continue with the planting of 2,500 seedlings 
in the park, ensuring the recovery of the mangrove 
VIPIS’ mangroves represent 21% of its total 
extension, made up of Rhizophora mangle (red 
mangrove), Avicennia germinans (salted mangrove), 
Laguncularia racemosa (yellow mangrove) and 
Conocarpus erectus (Zaragoza mangrove). However, 
over the decades, these ecosystems have faced 
multiple threats, such as deforestation, blocked 
streams, and increased salinity, leading to the loss 
of 56% of the original mangrove cover.
Our restoration work has a direct impact on the 
recovery of these ecosystems. The success of 
the process depends on ensuring the proper 
establishment of the planted trees and the 
restoration of water flow through the rehabilitated 
canals, which allows salinity levels to be controlled 
and mangrove regeneration to be encouraged.
In addition to the environmental benefits, this 
restoration project has generated positive impacts 
on nearby communities:
 S trengthening community work: restoration 
has promoted collaboration between the 
community, organizations and environmental 
authorities, generating a sense of shared 
responsibility in the protection of the ecosystem.
 B oosting the local economy: we have generated 
employment in planting and maintenance 
activities, in addition to promoting opportunities 
 P rotection against climate change: Mangrove 
recovery strengthens the resilience of 
communities by mitigating the effects of extreme 
weather events and protecting biodiversity.
This joint effort allows us to advance in the recovery 
and conservation of VIPIS, ensuring that this valuable 
ecosystem continues to provide its environmental 
services to the region and future generations.

Blue Planet National 
At Banco de Occidente, we created the Blue Planet 
National Ecology Award: Water, Principle of 
Life with the purpose of recognizing and exalting 
projects, programs and actions that contribute to 
the protection, conservation and recovery of water 
and the environment, as well as to the promotion 
of sustainable practices. For more than 30 years, 
we have been a benchmark in the private sector as 
promoters of the care of water and biodiversity.
We have been granting this recognition since 1993, 
and in October 2024 we proudly celebrated the 
16th edition. This award is held every two years, 
consolidating itself as a representative event in 
terms of environmental sustainability. Throughout 
its history, we have evaluated more than 3,600 
projects, reaffirming our commitment to sustainable 
selection process:

## Página 154
At Banco de Occidente, we believe that the 
development of our talent and the impact on 
communities are essential to achieve our strategic 
objectives and consolidate ourselves as a benchmark 
in sustainability. Our purpose is to generate value 
for our customers, employees and society.
Through an organizational culture based on equity, 
well-being, and professional growth, we strengthen 
our commitment to talent development and the 
creation of opportunities. Likewise, our relationship 
with communities is based on financial inclusion, 
education and the promotion of initiatives that 
generate a positive and sustainable impact.
This chapter details our actions in human capital, 
talent well-being, diversity, equity and inclusion, 
human rights, occupational health and safety, 
and commitment to communities and customers, 
pillars that allow us to advance our vision of being 
an increasingly sustainable and innovative bank.
## Página 155
Wellbeing and Motivation: 
Taking Care of Our People
At Banco de Occidente, we recognize that the well-being of our employees is key to 
their personal and professional development, as well as to the Bank’s success. For this 
reason, we implement initiatives that promote physical, mental and emotional health, 
creating a work environment where each person can reach their full potential.
Our programs are designed to positively impact not only employees, but also their 
families, ensuring a work-life balance. Through well-being strategies, we foster a 
culture of motivation, commitment and high performance, contributing to an enriching 
and sustainable work experience.
BdeO Mentoring Program:  
This program aims to accompany and promote the personal and 
professional development of Banco de Occidente employees, 
maximizing their skills and competencies within the organization. 
Through this program, key competencies such as leadership, 
communication skills, time management, innovation, result orientation, and 
attention to detail are developed. This positively impacts the performance 
of employees, which contributes to their personal and professional growth, 
and consequently, improves the overall results of the organization. During 
the period evaluated, 2.49% of our staff, equivalent to 175 employees, 
participated in the program, with an investment of $41,007 ,837 .
## Página 156
Advanced High Performance Commercial 
Program - The Master KAM:  
This program is designed to enhance the high performance of 
commercial leaders and teams in the Business and Corporate 
segments, through a practical and bottom-up training process, 
which contributes to the increase of productivity and commercial 
effectiveness. Some of the business impacts translate into the 
consolidation of commercial forces as a competitive advantage 
in the market, the assurance of the sustainability of commercial 
results, aligned with the Commercial Action Model and the increase 
in effectiveness in commercial objectives, improving relationships, 
advice and service. The initiative impacted 2.0% of the workforce 
(143 employees) with an investment of $341,747 ,060, including 
training, materials and event logistics.
Continuous Training Programs in partnership 
with Camacoes and Britcham: 
This continuous training program offers three key training 
actions, focused on improving the work skills of employees 
in critical areas such as: internal customer experience, 
disruptive thinking, and innovative strategies to retain 
talent. In addition, the trainings positively impact the personal 
and professional development of our employees, improving 
performance in their current roles and contributing to 
organizational success. Through a tender with SENA, we 
managed to train 5.2% of our workforce (368 employees) 
without generating additional costs.
The Leader’s Path - Team Building VP People: 
This leadership process is aimed at Area Managers, with the purpose 
of strengthening their self-leadership, team management and people 
management skills, which contributes to the achievement of business 
results and adaptation to change. Some of the business benefits translate into 
improved effective decision-making, strengthening leaders’ abilities to make 
strategic decisions, increasing team cohesion and organizational culture, and 
improving communication and collaboration between teams, contributing to a 
more harmonious and efficient work environment. During 2024, 25 employees 
participated in this initiative, representing 0.35% of our workforce, with an 
investment of $33,200,000.

Performance Appraisal 
The performance appraisal process that we manage 
at Banco de Occidente is based on management 
by objectives, which allows us to evaluate individual 
and organizational performance aligned with our 
strategic goals. This process is carried out through 
the Success Factors module, a tool that we provide to 
our employees to carry out an objective and efficient 
evaluation. Throughout this process, our employees 
have the opportunity to set goals that contribute to 
the success of the organization, and we work with 
them to ensure that each goal is aligned with the 
bank’s priorities.
It is relevant to mention that the closing stage of the 
performance assessment ends at the end of the first 
quarter of the year, so in this report we refer to the 
performance of the year 2023.
During the year, the Bank’s employees participated 
in various stages of the performance appraisal 
process, including: planning, initial meeting, valuation 
management, validation by the Human Talent area, 
and formalization. Each of these stages has a specific 
purpose, starting with the agreement of the objectives 
and ending with the definition of the individual results.
As a Bank, we are committed to accompanying 
our employees in each of these stages, ensuring 
compliance with the established deadlines. At the end 
of the process, we will obtain the individual results 
of the evaluated employees, which will be used as a 
strategic input in the management processes led by the 
Vice Presidency of Human and Administrative Talent, 
contributing to the strengthening of organizational 
## Página 159
During 2024, Banco de Occidente led two key 
moments in the performance appraisal process, 
designing specific strategies for each stage, adapted 
to the characteristics and needs of our employees.
In the first semester, we focused on the promotion 
and execution of the first phase of the process, 
which includes planning and the initial meeting. 
Through internal communications, such as emails, 
and open and voluntary live events, we provide 
detailed guidance and advice on this stage.
The planning phase is fundamental, as it allows 
our employees, in common agreement with their 
leaders, to define the objectives for the current year, 
establishing clear goals and assigning specific 
weights. Once the objectives were agreed, we held the 
initial meeting, a key instance of interaction between 
leader and employees, where our employees were 
able to identify strengths and areas of opportunity 
related to the fulfillment of the agreed objectives.
After the deadlines for the first phase, we focused 
on employees who joined after the established 
deadline, offering them personalized sessions to 
ensure that they understood the proper use of the 
performance management tool. This supplement was 
complemented with materials such as instructions, 
videos and emails, facilitating their effective 
integration into the process.
In the last quarter of the year, we began the deployment 
of strategies for the closure of the performance 
appraisal process. This stage covers management 
and assessment, key moments in which the strengths 
and opportunities of each employee are analyzed, 
always in line with the objectives set. The events led 
in this phase aimed to offer tools and methodologies 
that would guarantee objectivity when defining final 
grades and evaluating competencies. 
In addition, at Banco de Occidente we promote 
the evaluation of team performance. We know 
that collaborative work is essential to achieving 
organizational goals, so we evaluate not only 
individual performance, but also the effectiveness and 
impact of teams. This approach allows us to identify 
strengths and areas of opportunity within work teams, 
improving cohesion and collective performance. 
Team assessments encourage collaboration, ensuring 
that each member is aligned with the bank’s mission 
In 2024, we also incorporated agile conversations 
as part of the performance appraisal process. These 
conversations focus on continuous feedback,  
allowing employees and leaders to maintain a 
constant dialogue about the progress of the objectives, 
the challenges they face and the opportunities for 
improvement. Agile conversations encourage a 
proactive and flexible approach, adapting quickly 
to changes and needs that may arise throughout the 
year. These conversations allow to adjust objectives in 
real time and ensure that the performance appraisal 
process is always aligned with the expected results.
## Página 160
One of the most relevant aspects of the performance appraisal 
process is the alignment of functional objectives with key strategic 
elements such as the Balance Scorecard (BSC). This alignment 
allowed the organization to identify areas of intervention based 
on the data obtained from the comparison between the results of 
the performance appraisal and the BSC indicators.
At Banco de Occidente, we have a 90° performance appraisal 
system, which evaluates main elements: organizational objectives, 
functional objectives and competencies. Each of these elements has 
a specific weight assigned by the Human Development Management, 
with a total of 100% in the assessment form. In addition, there is a 
fourth element, called the development objective, whose weight is 
0%, but it is mandatory within the process; this objective is designed 
to encourage, individually, the creation of goals focused on the 
technical or behavioral development of our employees.
Finally, in 2023, we implemented the 360° 
assessment tool as a pilot for the agile 
scaling team, whose purpose was to 
measure the agile mindset of the cells that 
make up the team. This exercise allowed 
us to obtain a partial measurement of the 
expected behaviors to perform in their roles 
and their impact within their work cell.

Employees Wellness and 
At Banco de Occidente, we understand that the health and well-being 
of our employees are fundamental to organizational success. We are 
committed to creating an environment that promotes satisfaction, 
productivity and retention, offering programs and benefits that allow 
our employees to balance their work responsibilities with their personal 
needs. This includes flexible work arrangements, paid parental and 
care leave, as well as supportive spaces such as breastfeeding rooms. 
These initiatives not only strengthen the morale of our employees but 
also contribute to the reduction of absenteeism and turnover, favoring 
the attraction and retention of the best talent. As a result, we managed 
to improve our financial and non-financial performance indicators, 
driving sustainable growth and a more inclusive and balanced work 
environment for all.

## Página 163
Family and Personal 
One day off is granted per semester so that employees can spend time with their 
families. This benefit seeks to strengthen family ties and promote a more cohesive 
work environment. Although there is no exact measurement of usage, leaders 
are encouraged to support their teams in taking advantage of this day.
2 paid days are granted in addition to the maternity leave established by law. This contributes 
to the improvement in employees satisfaction and retention, supporting work-life balance.
Similarly, 2 paid days are granted in addition to the paternity leave established by 
law, encouraging active participation of fathers in the first days of their children’s lives.
Bereavement leave:  
In the event of the death of a close relative, additional paid days are granted according to the 
relationship (first degree of consanguinity: 1 additional day; second degree: leave established 
by law). This benefit seeks to provide emotional support and allow adequate time for mourning.
Birthday afternoon:  
Each employees can take a paid half working day on their birthday, choosing 
between morning or afternoon. This benefit promotes the well-being of 
employees, allowing them to enjoy personal time on a meaningful date.
## Página 164
Social Benefits and 
5 working days of leave are granted in case of marriage or common-
law union, supporting employees at key moments in their lives.
Paid days are granted in situations of family calamity, adapting 
to the needs of the employees according to the case.
Grants are granted for technical, technological and university studies, both for employees and 
for children of employees. In 2024, $1,488,936,884 was invested to benefit 2,342 employees.
Additional assistance includes support for ophthalmological expenses, birth, adoption, marriage, 
death of relatives, and deed. In total, $539,877 ,716 was invested for 1,030 employees.
Medical insurance:  
Medical insurance is provided that covers surpluses of the EPS and prepaid medical insurance for 
the employees and his family, benefiting 3,651 employees with an investment of $2,507 ,321,499.
A life and personal accident policy is offered to indemnify employees and their beneficiaries 
in the event of death, benefiting 6,794 employees with an investment of $1,800,112,618.

Variable Compensation
Our Variable Compensation Model is designed to 
drive high performance in commercial areas. Its 
purpose is to establish a system that reinforces the 
measurement culture and encourages progress in 
the execution of the strategy, ensuring the fulfillment 
of commercial objectives.
To achieve this, we have an evaluation scheme based 
on performance indicators of the sales team, which 
represents 19% of our total employees. Compensation 
(percentage in addition to the base salary earned for 
meeting goals) is managed on a monthly basis for 
Bar Advisors, Vehicle Executives, and Finance Center 
Advisors, while for Division Managers, Relationship 
Managers, Coordinators, Executives, Investment 
Managers, and Directors with business functions in 
the Vice Presidency of Businesses, Vice-Presidency 
of Personal Banking and Treasury Management, it 
is applied quarterly.
In 2024, the results reflect 
the effectiveness of the 
model and its impact on 
meeting our strategic goals.

Hiring and Turnover
I GRI 401-1; BdO-8 I
At Banco de Occidente, we understand that hiring new employees and managing staff turnover are fundamental 
elements to maintain a healthy and productive work environment. Through effective selection processes, 
we seek to integrate the team of employees with the talent and skills necessary to achieve the strategic 
objectives of the organization. At the same time, we manage staff turnover proactively, to minimize the loss 
of knowledge and experience, promoting stability and long-term commitment.
In this context, our focus is not only on attracting the best talent, but also on creating an environment in which 
our employees feel motivated, valued and with opportunities for growth within the Bank. In this way, we foster 
a strong organizational culture that allows for the continuous evolution and success of our institution.
Number and Rates of Hire
In 2024, we consolidated our internal mobility strategy, allowing 7 out of 10 vacancies to be filled by talent 
within the organization. Of the 2,151 vacancies opened during the year, 1,576 were filled by our own 
employees, reaching 73% of internal coverage. This result represents a significant advance compared 
to 2023, when the percentage was 57 .6%, that is, an increase of more than 15 percentage points in the 
promotion of internal talent.
These results reflect our commitment to the growth and career projection of our employees, strengthening 
their development within the organization and promoting a culture that values the retention and evolution of

Diversity, Equity, 
At Banco de Occidente we have a common purpose and we know that to achieve it we have a 
team that reflects our values and corporate identity. Respect, as the main value of our culture, is 
transversal to all our operations and reaffirms our commitment to the protection of human rights 
and the creation of diverse environments, free of discrimination, violence and harassment in 
the workplace. We guarantee the physical, mental and social well-being of our employees and 
stakeholders, in line with our Human Rights Policy, Internal Work Regulations and Code of Ethics 
Currently, we are part of Asobancaria’s Social Protocol, a voluntary agreement that promotes 
equity, diversity and inclusion in the Colombian financial sector. This protocol establishes good 
practices in four key strategies: internal culture, financial education and inclusion, value proposition 
and financial risk management.
Likewise, under our Human Rights Due Diligence approach, we incorporate diversity, equity and 
inclusion criteria in the Human Rights Policy, aligned with the United Nations Guiding Principles, 
as well as in the Code of Ethics and Conduct and the Internal Work Regulations. Our 2024 was

At Banco de Occidente, respect for Human Rights is a fundamental principle that 
guides our management and allows us to generate responsible and sustainable 
relationships with our stakeholders. Our commitment is aligned with international 
standards such as the United Nations Guiding Principles on Business and Human 
Rights and is embodied in our Human Rights Policy, which establishes guidelines 
to prevent and address risks related to child labor, forced labor, human trafficking, 
equal pay and non-discrimination, among other key aspects.
Our Human Rights due diligence approach extends to the entire organization, 
including our operations, suppliers, and business partners, with the goal of 
proactively identifying, assessing, and mitigating risks. To this end, we carry out 
systematic and periodic reviews that allow us to map the main challenges in our 
value chain and establish concrete measures for the prevention, mitigation and 
remediation of negative impacts.
In recent years, we have strengthened our evaluation processes by implementing 
tools that allow us to measure the percentage of activities evaluated, identify 
specific risks, and adopt mitigation and remediation plans in our own operations, 
contractors, Tier 1 suppliers, and joint ventures where we have a stake. In this 
chapter, we detail the results of our evaluations, the actions implemented and 
the mechanisms with which we ensure the protection and promotion of Human 
Rights in all our business activities.
Our Commitment to Human Rights
At Banco de Occidente, we reaffirm our commitment to the respect and promotion 
of Human Rights, aligning ourselves with internationally recognized standards and 
regulatory frameworks. Our Human Rights Policy establishes clear guidelines 
to prevent, mitigate, remediate, and repair the risks and impacts identified in 
our operations, the value chain, and in relation to all our stakeholders, including 
the Board of Directors, shareholders, employees, suppliers, allies, customers, 
communities, and the environment.
Our commitment is based on international principles such as:
 U niversal Declaration of Human Rights.
 Int ernational Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights.
 Int ernational Covenant on Civil and Political Rights.
 IL O Declaration of Fundamental Principles and Rights at Work.
 IL O Fundamental Conventions.
 Int ernational Convention on the Rights of the Child.
 C onvention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities.
 C onvention against Torture and Other Cruel, Inhuman or Degrading Treatment 
 Int ernational Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial Discrimination.
 C onvention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women.
 Int ernational Convention on the Protection of the Rights of All Migrant 
Employees and Members of Their Families.

business activities, including critical aspects such as the prevention of child labor, forced labor, human trafficking, 
freedom of association, the right to collective bargaining, equal remuneration, and non-discrimination. Among 
these commitments we highlight:

As part of our management approach, Banco de Occidente has implemented a structured human 
rights due diligence process,  aligned with the United Nations Guiding Principles on Business and 
Human Rights. This process allows us to identify, assess, mitigate, and remediate impacts on our 
business, operations, and supply chain.
Our Human Rights due diligence process includes the following phases:
Context analysis:  We review international standards, local regulations and 
best practices in the field.
Identification of risks and impacts: Through consultations with our 
stakeholders, we map the possible risks and impacts on Human 
Rights within our operations and value chain.
Risk and impact assessment and action plan : We assess 
the identified impacts and design mitigation and remediation 
Monitoring and follow-up: We periodically evaluate the 
effectiveness of the actions implemented to ensure compliance.
Communication and transparency: We share the progress 
of our human rights management with stakeholders, ensuring 
clear and accessible communication.
Review and continuous improvement: We adapt and strengthen 
our due diligence process based on lessons learned and changes in 
the regulatory and business environment.

At Banco de Occidente, we reaffirm our commitment 
to the well-being of our employees through a robust 
Occupational Health and Safety Management System 
(OH&S-MS) aligned with the highest standards. Our 
strategy not only responds to regulatory requirements, 
but also seeks to generate a positive impact on the 
organizational culture, promoting safe, healthy and 
sustainable work environments.
Occupational Health 
At Banco de Occidente, we are committed to the 
safety and well-being of our employees, contractors, 
and anyone under our supervision. Our Occupational 
Health and Safety policy is applicable to all our 
operations and complies with relevant national 
and international regulations, as well as applicable 
voluntary standards and collective agreements.
We encourage the consultation and participation 
of our employees and their representatives in 
the identification of risks, the implementation of 
preventive measures and the continuous improvement 
of our OSH management system. To this end, we set 
quantifiable objectives, prioritize action plans and 
promote a culture of prevention in all our areas of 
As part of our commitment to sustainability and 
improving organizational performance, we report 
our OSH progress within the framework of key 
indicators used in assessments such as the Dow 
Jones Sustainability Index (DJSI). This allows us to 
continuously evaluate and optimize our performance 
metrics, ensuring responsible management aligned 
with industry best practices.
Our Executive Management endorses and promotes the 
implementation of this policy, ensuring its integration 
into our corporate strategy and its alignment with 
our values of well-being and sustainability.
Our Occupational Health 
and Safety Program
At Banco de Occidente, we carry out periodic risk 
and hazard assessments in the field of Occupational 
Health and Safety (OSH) to identify and mitigate 
factors that may affect the well-being of our 
employees and contractors. We prioritize and 
integrate action plans with quantifiable objectives, 
aligned with our corporate strategy.
We have emergency prevention and response 
protocols, regular internal inspections and 
external audits under national and international 
standards and rules, ensuring compliance 
and continuous improvement of our OSH 
management system.
We investigate any injury, illness, or workplace 
incident in a structured manner to implement 
corrective actions. In addition, we offer OSH 
training to employees and third parties, 
promoting a culture of prevention. OSH 
criteria are incorporated into our contracting 
requirements, ensuring our partners’ 
commitment to safety.

prevention of musculoskeletal disorders, industrial

reintegration processes, emergency preparedness

risk management. In addition, we worked on the 
pregnant women and breastfeeding program, 
the communication and training plan in OSH, the 
strengthening of employees participation committees 
such as COPASST, the Coexistence Committee and 
the Road Safety Committee, and the program for 
suppliers and contractors.

Hazard identification, 
risk assessments and 
incident investigation
At our bank, we manage occupational health and 
safety through a structured approach based on 
hazard identification, risk assessment and incident 
investigation. We implement an Occupational Health 
and Safety Management System (OSHMS) aligned 
with local regulations and international standards, 
guaranteeing a safe work environment for our 
To identify hazards, we carry out periodic inspections 
at the facilities, surveys of employees and analysis 
of working conditions, to detect potential risks. 
We use qualitative and quantitative risk analysis 
methodologies to prioritize and mitigate threats.
In terms of risk assessment, we apply the risk 
matrix to classify and manage hazards related to 
ergonomic, psychosocial, biological and physical 
factors. In addition, we promote operational controls 
## Página 181
and specific action plans to minimize exposure to 
occupational risks.
Regarding incident investigation, we follow a 
standardized protocol that includes information 
gathering, root cause analysis, and establishing 
improvement plans. An internal committee analyzes 
incidents and accidents at work, ensuring the 
application of corrective and preventive measures 
to prevent their recurrence.
In addition, we carry out constant training in 
occupational safety, promote a culture of risk 
reporting, and work on the continuous improvement 
of the OSHMS to guarantee the well-being of our 
In our bank, we have a comprehensive occupational 
health program that contributes to the identification, 
prevention and minimization of occupational risks, 
guaranteeing the well-being of our employees. We 
implement a comprehensive rehabilitation program, 
through which we monitor and accompany employees 
who have health conditions that may generate 
prolonged disabilities (greater than 30 days) or that 
require restrictions or work recommendations.
In addition, we carry out periodic occupational 
medical examinations of the entire working population, 
ensuring early detection of risk factors and timely 
intervention. Every year, we carry out an occupational 
health diagnosis, analyzing the main findings of 
occupational assessments, which allows us to plan 
preventive activities and intervention strategies in 
the field of occupational medicine.
To ensure quality and access to these services, we 
work with a team of health professionals, including 
occupational physicians, physiotherapists, and 
occupational psychologists, who provide ongoing 
accompaniment. We also maintain strategic alliances 
with nationally certified providers for the provision 
of specialized medical services.

Employees training on 
EAt Banco de Occidente, occupational health and 
safety (OSH) is a fundamental pillar of our well-
being and occupational risk prevention strategy. To 
this end, we have implemented a comprehensive 
training program aimed at all our employees and 
employees who, although they are not a direct part of 
our organization, carry out their work in our facilities 
or under our supervision.
As part of our OSH management, we identify 
training needs through a methodology based on 
risk assessment and evaluation, where we analyze 
the specific hazards of each job. This process 
is complemented by the information obtained 
through the Epidemiological Surveillance System, 
occupational health diagnosis, investigations of 
occupational incidents and diseases, as well as 
analysis of the current epidemiological context. 
In this way, we ensure that our training is relevant 
and responds to the real working conditions of our 
The trainings are designed in conjunction with 
specialized professionals, both internal and 
external, including experts from our Occupational 
Risk Administrator (ARL), health service provider 
institutions (IPS) and strategic allies. These trainings 
can be given in face-to-face, virtual or hybrid mode, 
depending on the nature of the topics addressed. 
In addition, in some cases, theoretical-practical 
sessions are included to ensure a better appropriation 
Among the main trainings we offer is induction 
and re-induction in the Occupational Health and 
Safety Management System (OSHMS), aimed at 
all the bank’s employees, including providers of 
general, temporary, technology, surveillance and 
security services. In addition, we have specialized 
courses, such as training at heights for employees 
who perform work in this type of conditions, training 
in the safe handling of chemical substances for 
storage and logistics personnel, and the course in 
the proper use of personal protective equipment 
(PPE) for populations exposed to specific risks.
Another pillar of our training strategy is the training of 
the teams responsible for emergency management. 
On a voluntary basis, all employees can participate 
in the emergency brigade course, although for those 
who are an active part of these groups, training is 
mandatory. This training covers topics such as first 
aid, cardiopulmonary resuscitation (CPR) maneuvers, 
management of syncope, shock and seizures, care 
for metabolic pathologies such as diabetes and 
hypertension, fire control and evacuation plans. 
Similarly, the members of the Emergency Operating 
Committee (COE) receive training on roles and 
responsibilities in crisis management, as well as in 
the identification and response to early warnings in 
our facilities nationwide.
In the field of workplace well-being, we promote 
training in ergonomics, active breaks and postural 
hygiene, aimed at employees in administrative areas,

The rate of occupational accidents stood at 4.1, reflecting an increase compared to the previous year. This increase is directly 
related to the greater number of reported events, which in turn may be a consequence of the growth in our workforce, and 
therefore a greater exposure to operational risks.
In the case of our contractors, the accident rate remained at zero, which shows adequate safety management in outsourced 
activities. In the combined total of employees and contractors, the rate stood at 4.1, which reaffirms the need to continue 
strengthening our strategies for the prevention and mitigation of occupational risks.
In terms of occupational diseases, in 2024 two cases were reported in our workforce, which represents a reduction compared 
to the previous year. This decrease was related to better identification and management of occupational risk factors, as well 
as the strengthening of ergonomics, active breaks and health monitoring.
For contractors, the rate of occupational diseases remained at zero, and in the total (employees and contractors), the number 
of cases also decreased compared to 2023. However, we continue to strengthen our occupational health initiatives to minimize 
the incidence of work-related diseases and improve the quality of life of our employees.
The accident severity index for our employees stood at 3.80, which represents a 
reduction compared to the previous year. This behavior is associated with a decrease 
in days of disability due to work accidents, which is related to better risk management 
and effective return to work processes.
For our contractors, the severity rate remains at zero, reflecting an adequate management 
of safety standards in the execution of their activities. In the combined total of employees 
and contractors, the severity index reached 3.78, showing an improvement over the 
These results highlight the positive impact of 
our preventive initiatives and the effectiveness 
of the safety protocols implemented, which 
have allowed us to reduce the impact of 
accidents in terms of days of disability.

strategies in outsourced processes. In the combined total, the frequency index reached 0.81, 
prompting us to further strengthen our accident prevention training and awareness initiatives.
Accident Frequency
The absenteeism rate for employees in 2024 was 14.23, reflecting an increase 
compared to the previous year. This increase is mainly associated with a greater 
number of days of disability due to common events, which highlights the 
need to continue promoting the comprehensive well-being of our employees, 
including aspects of physical and mental health.
For contractors, the absenteeism rate reached 76.42, influenced by the increase 
in days of disability due to common events. This translates into the importance 
of continuing to strengthen the well-being and health conditions for this group, 
in line with our occupational health and safety standards. 
In the combined total of employees and contractors, the absenteeism rate 
stood at 14.30, which motivates us to continue promoting disease prevention 
initiatives and the strengthening of healthy habits in the work environment.

Banking Correspondents
Our Correspondent Banking channel has been key 
to expanding access to financial services in rural 
communities and disadvantaged sectors, where the 
presence of bank branches is limited. During 2024, 
we managed to increase the number of service points 
in hard-to-reach regions, going from 53,000 in 2023 
to 90,000 by the end of the year. This facilitated 
essential transactions such as bill payments, PILA, 
withdrawals, and deposits, as well as boosting the 
banking penetration of the Dale! digital wallet in 
the correspondent Point of Payment, with more 
than 59,000 connections in the last four months of 
the year. With these actions, we have reduced the 
geographical and economic barriers that exclude 
many people from the formal financial system.
To ensure that our services are accessible and 
understandable to everyone, we have worked 
on simplifying and standardizing processes at 
correspondent banking points. We prioritize the 
training of correspondents, who are the first point 
of contact with communities, ensuring that they 
provide clear and effective guidance. We also design 
materials and signage in an accessible language, 
making it easy to use our services regardless of the 
educational level of the users. Although we have 
not yet implemented specific financial education 
programs with the communities, we focus on making 
our service points work as an extension of the 
Bank, bringing services closer in a practical and 
understandable way.
Although the Banking Correspondent Unit has not 
developed specific financial education programs, 
at a global level we promote educational initiatives 
through communication campaigns. These seek 
to raise awareness among customers about the 
## Página 189
responsible use of credit and savings, indirectly reaching the communities served 
by banking correspondents. In this sense, correspondents play a fundamental role 
in making it easier for users to understand how to carry out basic transactions 
safely and effectively, reinforcing our commitment to financial inclusion.
We measure the social impact of our banking correspondents through key 
indicators such as the increase in Dale!’s banking penetration and transaction 
volume. In 2024, we achieved a 14% growth in transactions and  1,987% in 
Dale!’s banking penetration, contributing significantly to the financial inclusion 
of these communities.
In terms of sustainability, in 2024 we began the implementation of the Stand-in 
initiative, designed to ensure the operational continuity of banking correspondents 
even in cases of disruptions in our systems. With this system, customers can 
make payments and other transactions without being affected by operational 
outages, ensuring a smooth and reliable experience. In addition to improving 
efficiency, this initiative reduces the need for additional travel for users, reinforcing 
our commitment to accessibility and sustainability in financial services.
We also implemented several innovations in our Correspondent Banking channel

 Migr ation of the dedicated SuperGIROS and Point of Payment channel,

 P hase 2 of SuperGIROS, which enabled new services such as cardless

CX Awards: Recognizing

At Banco de Occidente, we are committed to offering 
an exceptional experience to our customers. As part of 
this commitment, every year we hold the CX Awards, 
an event in which we recognize the areas, offices 
and employees that have implemented successful 
initiatives and have generated a positive impact on 
The selection of the awarded projects is made through 
a call open to all areas of the bank. During this 
phase, the areas nominate the projects implemented 
throughout the year that have significantly improved 
the customer experience. A specialized team evaluates 
each initiative and defines the finalists. Subsequently, 
an evaluation jury analyzes the projects and selects 
the winners based on predefined criteria. Winners are 
announced and recognized at the annual customer 
Categories evaluated
The CX Awards include six categories, each 
highlighting a key aspect in the transformation of 
the customer experience:
 B est Projects: We recognize teams that 
have implemented innovative solutions and 
transformed key moments in our customers’ 
journey. These projects have used customer 
experience tools to generate tangible impacts 
on the bank’s profitability and customer 
 B est ENSI (Internal Satisfaction Level): We 
celebrate areas that have achieved maximum 
internal customer satisfaction. This recognition 
highlights the synergy between areas, teamwork, 
accessibility and empathy in service.
 W OW Offices: We recognize offices that 
have excelled in exceptional customer service 
performance. The evaluation considers 
satisfaction studies, unknown customer results, 
participation in customer experience campaigns, 
and implementation of improvement plans.
 W OW Employees: We recognize those 
employees who have exceeded expectations, 
creating unforgettable experiences for our 
customers. These employees have been praised 
by customers and internal teams, leaving an 
indelible mark on every interaction.
 B est Managers: We distinguish commercial 
managers with the highest levels of 
recommendation from our clients. Their advice, 
solutions, accompaniment and empathy have 
made them benchmarks within the bank.
 Exper ience Ambassadors: A group of employees 
from different areas who inspire the organization 
to achieve memorable experiences. They 
participate in the co-creation of solutions to 
challenges identified in the customer experience 
and promote best practices in their day-to-day

Customer Recommendation 
At Banco de Occidente, customer experience is 
a strategic priority. Our overall NPS has remained 
stable in recent years, reaching 68% in 2024, close 
to our goal of 70%. In Business Banking, we achieved 
an increase of 2 percentage points, reaching the 
best NPS in the last four years and reflecting an 
improvement in the perception of our business 
customers. In Personal Banking, the indicator 
remained stable compared to 2023, although we 
continue to work on opportunities for improvement 
to strengthen our customers’ recommendation and 
achieve the proposed goals.
To better understand the perception of our customers, 
we carry out constant measurements that allow us to 
identify strengths and areas of opportunity. We look 
at what our customers value most and the critical 
aspects we need to focus on to reduce friction in 
the experience. Our promoter clients highlight the 
## Página 192
quality of our service and the portfolio of products and services, key factors in loyalty. On the other hand, 
passive and detractor customers show a lower recommendation when they perceive that we are not timely 
and close enough in service, or when they encounter difficulties with our products, services and channels.
In 2024, we evaluated the satisfaction of 4,584 customers, representing 0.46% of our customer base, with 
samples selected under statistical criteria that guarantee representativeness and a margin of error equal 
to or less than 5%. This methodology, endorsed by IZO, an international expert provider of quantitative 
measurements, ensures the reliability of our results.
Specifically, we attended to  252,160 requests, 
resolving 250,849 of them (99.48%), and managed 
24,560 complaints, of which 24,492 were resolved 
(99.72%).
These results reflect our commitment to transparency, 
continuous improvement and customer satisfaction.

Strengthening access to water 
and sanitation in vulnerable 
communities with UNICEF
At Banco de Occidente, we are committed to the social and 
economic development of the country’s most vulnerable 
communities. In line with this purpose, for three years we have 
strengthened our alliance with UNICEF and the WASH (Water, 
Sanitation and Hygiene) program, through which we promote 
a donation program that has allowed us to generate a real 
impact in La Guajira. Thanks to this joint effort, we have brought 
drinking water and better sanitation conditions to more than 
26 communities in the municipalities of Manaure and Uribia, 
transforming their environment and quality of life.
UNICEF’s work is critical to ensuring children’s rights in more 
than 190 countries and territories, and in Colombia, its focus on 
water, sanitation and hygiene has led to solutions tailored to the 
needs of the most vulnerable communities. Through the WASH 
program, we work so that children and adolescents have access 
to drinking water and can grow up in healthy environments that 
promote their well-being and integral development.
Our support has been key to the construction of six new water 
supply systems, contributing to sustainable access to basic 
sanitation services. In 2024, we allocated $283,703,267 to this 
program with the valuable contribution of 1,122 customers, and 
since 2022, we have donated a total of $1,910,229,925. Thanks 
to this joint effort, we have been able to:
 Gener ate impact in 1,028 people, including 343 children 
and adolescents, in 24 communities.
 P rovide access for 4,100 people to basic sanitation, of 
which 1,000 live in emergency contexts.
 C ertify 1,500 people as free of open defecation.
 12, 000 people in humanitarian emergency contexts with 
access to safe drinking water and quality services.
 14  strengthened health centers with access to water, 
sanitation and hygiene, promoting the right to health of 
children and adolescents.
 20 ,600 menstruating girls and adolescents benefited from 
menstrual hygiene supplies and education, of which 20,000 
live in humanitarian emergency contexts.

This impact transcends access to basic services, 
since having drinking water and adequate sanitation 
allows other fundamental rights, such as health, 
nutrition, education and child protection, to be 
guaranteed. Improving conditions in schools and 
communities not only prevents diseases and reduces 
school dropouts but also promotes a safer and more 
dignified environment for the development of children 
to the well-being of communities and will continue 
to work together with UNICEF to expand our impact, 
contributing to the construction of a more sustainable

or in-kind resources with the aim of generating a 
positive impact on communities and populations in 
vulnerable situations. These donations are part of our 
three strategic pillars: environmental conservation, 
education for development and conscious social 
Through this approach, we seek to strengthen 
initiatives that promote respect for fundamental rights, 
contribute to the improvement of people’s quality of 
life and foster the sustainable development of the 
regions in which we have a presence. Each donation 
responds to our commitment to generate value in 
society and support the progress of communities 
through access to opportunities that allow their 
well-being and growth.
Our donations are aligned with our corporate purpose 
of making the development of people, the growth of 
businesses and the transformation of the country a 
reality. Through these contributions, we expand our 
impact to territories and populations that we do 
not necessarily reach with our financial operation, 
allowing the consolidation of relationships of trust 
with communities and social organizations.
The identification of needs in the territories where 
we operate facilitates the establishment of strategic 
alliances and the definition of initiatives that 
contribute to improving the living conditions of the 
population, promoting long-term solutions and 
generating shared value with the different actors

who, from different fronts, have contributed to strengthening our

governance criteria in our management.

INFORME DE ASEGURAMIENTO LIMITADO INDEPENDIENTE  
Hemos sido contratados por la Dirección de Banco de Occidente S.A. (en adelante “El Banco”) para llevar a cabo un 
trabajo de aseguramiento limitado sobre la información detallada en el Anexo A (en adelante, información objeto de 
aseguramiento), incluida en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad para el año terminado el 31 de diciembre de 2024.    
Nuestro compromiso de aseguramiento limitado se realizó únicamente en relación con la información seleccionada  
de sostenibilidad incluida en el Anexo A. Nuestro informe de aseguramiento no se extiende a información de períodos 
anteriores ni a otra información no incluida en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad 2024, ni a otra información  
relacionada a dicho Informe que pudiera contener imágenes, audios o videos.   
Criterios aplicados por Banco de Occidente S.A.  
Los criterios utilizados por la administración  de El Banco para preparar la información objeto de  aseguramiento 
detallada en el Anexo A e incluida en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad 2024 fueron establecidos considerando los 
conceptos, requerimientos y principios de:   
• Los estándares de la Global Reporting Initiative (GRI) 2021 en su opción de uso “Con referencia GRI”.   
• Los criterios definidos por El Banco para la metodología del proceso de análisis de doble materialidad vigente en  
• Los criterios definidos por El Banco para los indicadores propios 2024.   
Responsabilidades de la administración de Banco de Occidente S.A.  sobre la información objeto de 
aseguramiento incluida en el Informe de Sostenibilidad 2024   
La administración de El Banco es responsable por la elaboración y presentación de la información objeto de 
aseguramiento incluida en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad 2024, de acuerdo con los criterios mencionados en el 
párrafo anterior. Esta responsabilidad incluye el diseño, la implementación y el mantenimiento del control interno  
relevante para la preparación de la información objeto de aseguramiento que esté libre de errores materiales, ya sea 
debido a fraude o error.    
Responsabilidades de BDO  
Nuestra responsabilidad es expresar una conclusión de aseguramiento limitado sobre la información objeto de 
aseguramiento, con base en los procedimientos que hemos efectuado y la evidencia que hemos obtenido.  Hemos 
llevado a cabo nuestro trabajo de aseguramiento limitado de acuerdo con los lineamientos de la Norma Internacional de 
Encargos de Aseguramiento ISAE3000 (Revisada), Encargos de Aseguramiento distintos de la Auditoría o de la Revisión 
de Información Financiera Histórica emitida por el International Auditing And Assurance Standards Board (IAASB).   
Esta norma exige que concluyamos si ha llegado a nuestro conocimiento algún hecho que nos haga pensar que la  
declaración de la dirección no se presenta fielmente, en todos sus aspectos significativos. En un encargo de 
aseguramiento limitado, el profesional ejerciente lleva a cabo procedimientos (consistentes principalmente en 
realizar indagaciones a la dirección y a otras personas de la entidad, según proceda, y en aplicar procedimientos  
analíticos) y evalúa la evidencia obtenida.     
Los procedimientos que realizamos se basaron en nuestro juicio profesional e incluyeron indagaciones, 
entendimiento y observación de los procesos realizados y evidencias, recálculos, inspección de documentos, 
procedimientos analíticos, evaluación de la idoneidad de los métodos de cuantificación y políticas de informes y  
acuerdo o conciliación con los registros subyacentes.   
Dadas las circunstancias del compromiso, hemos realizado los siguientes procedimientos:  
a)   A través de indagaciones, se obtuvo una comprensión del entorno de control y sistemas de información de El 
Banco relevantes, pero no evaluamos el diseño de las actividades de control particulares ni obtuvimos  
evidencia sobre su implementación, ni probamos su efectividad operativa.   
b)   Entendimiento de las herramientas utilizadas para generar, agregar y reportar la información objeto de  
aseguramiento mediante indagaciones con los responsables de los procesos relacionados.   
c)  Entendimiento, indagación con los representantes delegados por la administración y verificación en sí, del  
proceso llevado a cabo por El Banco en 2024 para la elaboración / actualización de su análisis de doble  
materialidad vigente, incluida la participación de sus grupos de interés en este proceso.   
d)   Entrevistas con el personal de El Banco, para comprender su negocio y el proceso de preparación del  
Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad 2024.   
e)   Entrevistas con el personal de El Banco a nivel corporativo, responsables de la información a reportar, para 
comprender el proceso de recolección, consolidación y presentación de la información objeto de 
f)  Comprobación de los criterios de cálculo y su aplicación adecuada, de acuerdo con las metodologías 
descritas en los criterios de los indicadores objeto de aseguramiento, según alcance indicado en el Anexo A.   
g)  Realización de procedimientos analíticos para respaldar la razonabilidad de los datos.  
h)   Comparación de la información presentada en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad con la información  
correspondiente a las fuentes subyacentes relevantes para determinar si la misma ha sido incluida  en el 
Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad.   
i)  Análisis de los procesos de recolección y de control interno de los datos cuantitativos reflejados en el 
Informe, en cuanto a la confiabilidad de la información, utilizando procedimientos analíticos y pruebas de 
verificación con base en muestreos.   
j)  Lectura de la información incluida en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad, para compararla frente a los  
criterios definidos por los estándares GRI 1 – Fundamentos, GRI 2 - Contenidos Generales y GRI 3 -Temas 
Materiales aplicables según la declaración de uso definida por El Banco. Procedimiento efectuado con base en 
la versión del Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad 2024 suministrada por El Banco a BDO el día 21 de febrero 
k)  Aplicación  de  pruebas  sustantivas  sobre  una  base  selectiva  aleatoria  de  la  información  objeto  de 
aseguramiento, elaborada por la administración, para determinar los estándares e indicadores y corroborar que 
los datos se hayan medido, registrado, recopilado e informado adecuadamente a través de:   
i.  Inspección de políticas y procedimientos establecidos por El Banco.   
ii.  Inspección de documentos soporte de origen interno y externo.   
iv.  Comparaciones de los contenidos presentados por la Administración con lo establecidos en la sección  
de criterios de este informe.   
En el Anexo A se detalla la información objeto de aseguramiento incluida en el alcance de nuestro trabajo.  
Nuestro  encargo  de  aseguramiento  limitado  se  realizó  solamente  con  respecto  a  la  información  objeto  de 
aseguramiento incluida en el Anexo A, por el año terminado el 31 de diciembre de 2024; y no hemos realizado ningún 
procedimiento con respecto de años anteriores, proyecciones y metas futuras, o cualquier otro elemento de otra  
información incluida en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad por el año terminado el 31 de diciembre de 2024 y,  
por lo tanto, no expresamos una conclusión al respecto.   
Los procedimientos aplicados en un encargo de aseguramiento limitado varían en cuanto a su naturaleza y momento 
de aplicación, y son de menor alcance que en el caso de un encargo de aseguramiento razonable y, en consecuencia, el 
nivel de fiabilidad obtenido en un encargo de aseguramiento limitado es sustancialmente inferior al que se habría  
obtenido de haberse realizado un encargo de aseguramiento razonable.   
## Página 206
Consideramos que la evidencia obtenida es suficiente y apropiada para proveer una base para nuestra conclusión de 
aseguramiento limitado.   
Independencia y gestión de calidad  
Hemos cumplido con los requerimientos éticos y de independencia del código de ética profesional del contador 
público emitido por el International Ethics Standard Board for Accountants (IESBA), el cual se basa en los principios de  
integridad,  objetividad,   competencia   profesional   y  debido   cuidado,   confidencialidad   y  comportamiento 
Nuestra firma BDO Audit S.A.S BIC aplica el International Standard on Quality Management (“ISQM”) 1 y, por lo 
tanto, mantiene un  sistema integral de  control de calidad que incluye políticas y  procedimientos documentados 
relacionados con el cumplimiento de requisitos éticos, estándares profesionales y requisitos de ley y regulaciones  
Limitaciones inherentes del encargo de aseguramiento   
La información de sostenibilidad seleccionada está sujeta a incertidumbre inherente debido al uso de información no 
financiera, la cual es objeto de mayores limitaciones inherentes que la información financiera dada la naturaleza de los 
métodos utilizados para determinar, calcular, hacer muestreos o estimar dicha información. En la preparación de la 
información selecciona la entidad efectúa interpretaciones cualitativas sobre la relevancia, la materialidad y  la 
exactitud de la información que están sujetas a supuestos y juicios.   
Conclusión del aseguramiento limitado  
Basándonos en los procedimientos que hemos realizado y en las evidencias que obtuvimos, no ha llegado a nuestro  
conocimiento ninguna situación que nos lleve a pensar que la información objeto de aseguramiento indicada en el  
Anexo A de este informe, y que a su vez fue incluida en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad para el año terminado el 
31 de diciembre de 2024 de Banco de Occidente S.A., no ha cumplido de conformidad con lo establecido en la sección 
Restricción del uso del Informe   
Nuestro informe se emite exclusivamente con el propósito expuesto en el primer párrafo y no debe utilizarse para  
ningún otro propósito ni ser distribuido a otras partes por separado. Este informe se refiere solamente a los asuntos  
mencionados en las secciones precedentes y la información objeto de aseguramiento incluida en el Anexo A y no se  
extiende a ninguna otra información financiera y no financiera incluida en el Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad de  
Banco de Occidente S.A. para el año terminado el 31 de diciembre de 2024, ni a sus estados financieros, tomados en 
BDO Audit S.A.S. BIC entrega a Banco de Occidente S.A., a través de un informe adicional, las recomendaciones de 
acción para la futura preparación del Informe de Gestión y Sostenibilidad, que no modifican la conclusión expresada 
en este informe, buscando buscan fortalecer el proceso de construcción, gestión, medición, revisión, reporte y  
comunicación de los indicadores de sostenibilidad de El Banco.

19 GRI 2-1 Organizational Details
At Banco de Occidente we are a private financial institution. No government entity or organization 
related to state activities owns an equity interest in our company. Our main shareholder is Grupo 
Aval Acciones y Valores S.A., which as of December 31, 2023 had a 72.27% stake.

GRI 2-2 Entities included in the 
Sustainability reporting.
The information reported focuses on Banco de Occidente S.A. Although we mention our affiliates (FiduOccidente, Banco 
de Occidente de Panamá, Occidental Bank Barbados and Nexa BPO) in business performance, the specific sustainability 
data does not include these entities. Currently, we have not defined the limits and coverage of environmental and social 
indicators, including specific climate indicators in our affiliates.  We are in the process of evaluating how to include this 
information in future reports to ensure greater clarity and transparency in the scope of our sustainability reporting.

64 GRI 201-1 Direct Economic Value 
Generated and Distributed
Chapter on Responsible Growth and Comprehensive Risk Management; Financial outlook and stock market performance.
Change in the ROI Methodology: to ensure compliance with the requirements of the Dow Jones 
Sustainability Index (DJSI), we made an update to the formula used to calculate the Return on 
Investment in Human Capital (HC-ROI). In this new methodology, we make sure to:
Total income: includes the total income received by the company before making any 
deductions, including interest and valuation income, income from commissions and fees, net 
income from financial assets or liabilities held for trading, and other net income.
Total operating expenses: are reported in line with accepted accounting and financial reporting standards, 
including general administrative expenses, depreciation and amortization expenses, personnel expenses, 
interest and similar expenses, commission and fee expenses, and other operating expenses.
Total employees-related expenses: Considers all labor costs, including salaries, 
benefits, training programs, pensions, and severance payments.
Given this adjustment in the methodology, the historical data have been recalculated, which 
has generated changes in the previously reported values. HC ROI result recalculated for the last 
It is observed that in 2020 there was a significantly high value compared to the following years. This was related to 
extraordinary factors, such as financial optimization strategies, impacts derived from the pandemic and/or structural 
changes in the bank. From 2021 onwards, the HC ROI stabilizes in a more consistent range, with a decline in 2022 (3.43) 
and a gradual recovery in subsequent years (3.65 in 2023 and 3.91 in 2024). This behavior demonstrates a positive 
trend in the efficiency of the use of human capital, which we highlight for improvements in productivity, optimization 
of labor costs and the strengthening of human talent strategies. This analysis allows us to have a clearer view of the 
impact of human capital on the bank’s profitability, ensuring alignment with international sustainability standards.

FN-CB-230a.1 (1) Number of 
data breaches, (2) percentage 
involving personally identifiable 
information (PII), (3) number 
of affected account holders
In 2024 we had an incident related to the violation of data privacy, in this case, a complaint was received 
from a customer who found on the Scribd platform a document linked to the Bank that contained 119 
records, of which 29 corresponded to active customers, after receiving the alert, an investigation was 
carried out by the security area,  and there was no evidence of fraud linked to these clients, the document 
was removed from the platform and a complaint was filed with the Attorney General's Office against the 
former official involved, who worked in one of our affiliates, this incident was handled in accordance with our 
security protocols, minimizing the impact and guaranteeing the protection of our clients' information. 
 Inf ormation security, 
system availability
FN-CB-230a.2 Description of 
the approach to identifying and 
addressing data security risks
At the Bank, we identify and prioritize critical services through the Business Impact Analysis (BIA) exercise, 
which allows us to manage the risks associated with the processes and technologies involved, developing 
action plans that seek to reduce residual risk and achieve the acceptable level of risk, we have an information 
security and cybersecurity governance model,  supported by policies and procedures, such as the Homogeneous 
Information Protection Standard (#AVBO. NOSI. SI.005), and we ensure compliance through tools such as DLP 
(Data Loss Prevention), IAM (Identity & Access Management) and PAM (Privileged Access Management).

monetary losses resulting from

unfair competition, market 
manipulation, malpractice 
or other related financial 
industry laws or regulations
During 2024 we had 43 cases related to fraud against customers (electronic fraud that affected 
account deposits and TC, consumption not recognized with TC and payment of checks with a forged 
signature), in which we were convicted or entered into conciliatory agreements for $387,707,538.

136 GRI 305-5 GHG Emission Reductions
Restatement: We establish the year 2022 as our issuance baseline at Banco de Occidente, due to the stability and 
verification of the data obtained for that period. For the years 2022 and 2023, we have carried out a Re-expression of the 
information presented in our sustainable management report since the measurement of our carbon footprint was verified 
and audited by ICONTEC, which led us to a recalculation of the emissions generated in Scope 1 and 3. For this reason, 
the information is subject to a recalculation that considers data from the IPCC's AR6 supplementary material, related 
to the confirmation of the Global Warming Potential for Scope 1 (refrigerants). In addition, Resolution 40447 of 2022 of 
the Ministry of Mines and Energy updates the fuel blending percentages in motor gasoline and anhydrous ethanol from 
90% to 96%, which modifies the Scope 1 (fuels) and Scope 3 (outsourced transportation) information. This recalculation 
increased our emissions of:   
Total emissions: a total of 9,039.84 emissions in 2022 and 7,395.29 emissions in 2023.
